management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationPushover\nPushover\n\nThe Pushover modules allow you to send messages and interact with the Pushover API.\n\nGetting Stared with Pushover\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Pushover account\n\nA valid device\n\nA registered application\n\nIn order to use Pushover with Make, you must have a Pushover account. If you do not have one, you can create one at pushover.net.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Pushover to Make\n\nTo connect your Pushover account to Make, you need your User Key and an API Token.\n\nLog in to your Pushover account.\n\nYou can find your User Key on the homepage.\n\nTo obtain an API Token, you must register an application. Scroll to the bottom of the page and click Create an Application/API Token.\n\nConfigure the application how you'd like. Click Create Application.\n\nGo to your newly created application to find the API Token.\n\nIn Make, choose the Pushover module you want to use. Next to Connection, click Add.\n\nEnter your User Key and API Token in the respective fields.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have established the connection.\n\nActions\nSend a Message\n\nSends the written message to your pushover devices.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pushover account.\n\n\n\n\nMessage\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body of your message. Messages are currently limited to 1024 characters.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title of your message. The title is currently limited to 250 characters.\n\nNote\n\nIf you don't specify a title, the application's name will show by default.\n\n\n\n\nHTML\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to format your message with HTML tags. If Yes, the normal message content in your message parameter will display as HTML. May not be used together with monospace.\n\n\n\n\nMonospace\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to enable monospace messages. May not be used if html is used, and vice versa.\n\n\n\n\nDevice\n\n\t\n\nChoose the name of one of your devices to send just to that device, instead of all devices.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a supplementary URL to show with your message.\n\n\n\n\nURL Title\n\n\t\n\nEnter a title for the URL specified as the url parameter, otherwise just the URL is shown.\n\n\n\n\nTimestamp\n\n\t\n\nEnter a timestamp to show to the message receiver. See the list of supported date and time parameters.\n\nNote\n\nIn some cases, such as when messages have been queued on a remote server before reaching the Pushover servers, or delivered to Pushover out of order, this default timestamping may cause a confusing order of messages when viewed on the user's device. For these scenarios, your app may send messages to the API with the timestamp parameter set to the time of the original message.\n\n\n\n\nPriority\n\n\t\n\nSelect the priority of your message and how the message is presented to the receiver.\n\nNo Notification / Alert\n\nConsidered the lowest priority and does not generate any notification.\n\nSend as a Quiet Notification\n\nConsidered low priority and does not generate any sound or vibration, but still generates a popup/scrolling notification depending on the client operating system.\n\nDefault User's Settings\n\nMessages trigger sound, vibration, and display an alert according to the user's device settings.\n\nBypass User's Quiet Hours\n\nHigh priority messages that bypass a user's quiet hours. These messages will always play a sound and vibrate (if the user's device is configured to) regardless of the delivery time.\n\nRepeat Until the User has Acknowledged\n\nSimilar to high-priority notifications, but they repeat until the notification is acknowledged by the user.\n\n\n\n\nSound\n\n\t\n\nSelect the sound to play when receiving notifications, rather than the standard Pushover tone. You can sample the full list o available sounds here.\n\n\n\n\nFile\n\n\t\n\nChoose whether to add any attachments to your message.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Pushover account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.pushover.net. For example: /1/users/validate.json\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Pushover API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST to create a new entry.\n\nPUT to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH to make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE to delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Users\n\nThe following API call returns all the users from your Pushover account:\n\nURL: /1/users/validate.json\n\nMethod: POST\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body. Our example returned 1 user:\n\nPushover\nGetting Stared with Pushover\nConnecting Pushover to Make\nActions\nSend a Message\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Users\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
  },

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationMicrosoft Teams\nMicrosoft Teams \n\nWith Microsoft Teams modules in Make, you can monitor, list, create, update, delete, and retrieve teams and channels in your Microsoft Teams account.\n\nTo use the Microsoft Teams modules, you must have a Microsoft business account. You also should be an admin of the account and Microsoft Office 365 Premium must be activated for your admin business account. You can create an account at https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/business.\n\nRefer to the Microsoft Teams API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Microsoft Teams to Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Microsoft Teams module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional: Click Show advanced settings and enter your custom app client credentials.\n\nFor more information, refer to the Microsoft Teams documentation regarding client credentials. If requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/microsoft-teams.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Microsoft Teams modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nTeam\n\nYou can watch, list, retrieve, create, update teams and create and update teams for groups with the following modules.\n\nWatch Teams\nList Joined Teams\nList All Teams & Groups\nGet Team\nCreate Office 365 Group\nUpdate Team\nCreate Team\nDelete Team or Group\nChannel\n\nYou can list, retrieve, create, update, and delete channels with the following modules.\n\nList Channels\nGet a Channel\nCreate Channel\nUpdate Channel\nDelete Channel\nMessage\n\nYou can watch and send messages and replies with the following modules.\n\nWatch Messages\nWatch New Replies\nSend a Message\nReply to a Channel Message\nMember\n\nYou can add members to teams and to groups with the following modules.\n\nAdd a Member\nAdd a Member to a Group\nOnline Meeting\n\nYou can create, retrieve, update, and delete online meetings with the following modules.\n\nCreate an Online Meeting\nUpdate an Online Meeting\nGet an Online Meeting\nDelete an Online Meeting\nOther\n\nYou can search users, retrieve users' statuses, and call APIs with the following modules.\n\nSearch Users\nGet User's Presence\nMake an API Call\nPermissions Information for Microsoft Teams\nMicrosoft Teams\nConnect Microsoft Teams to Make\nTeam\nWatch Teams\nList Joined Teams\nList All Teams & Groups\nGet Team\nCreate Office 365 Group\nUpdate Team\nCreate Team\nDelete Team or Group\nChannel\nList Channels\nGet a Channel\nCreate Channel\nUpdate Channel\nDelete Channel\nMessage\nWatch Messages\nWatch New Replies\nSend a Message\nReply to a Channel Message\nMember\nAdd a Member\nAdd a Member to a Group\nOnline Meeting\nCreate an Online Meeting\nUpdate an Online Meeting\nGet an Online Meeting\nDelete an Online Meeting\nOther\nSearch Users\nGet User's Presence\nMake an API Call\nPermissions Information for Microsoft Teams\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationPhaxio\nPhaxio\n\nThe Phaxio modules allow you to create, send, resend, and cancel as fax in your Phaxio account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Phaxio account\n\nIn order to use Phaxio with Make, it is necessary to have a Phaxio account. If you do not have one, you can create a Phaxio account at https://www.phaxio.com/.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Phaxio to Make\n\nTo connect your Phaxio account to Make, you need to obtain your API Key and API Secret.\n\n1. Login to your Phaxio account.\n\n2. From the left menu, click API Keys.\n\n3. Copy the API Key and API Secret to your clipboard.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the Phaxio module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n6. In the API Key and API Secret fields, enter the details copied in step 3 respectively.\n\n7. Click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nActions\nCancel Fax\n\nCancels a fax.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Phaxio account.\n\n\n\n\nFax ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Fax ID you want to cancel.\n\nCreate and Send Fax\n\nCreate and sends a fax.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Phaxio account.\n\n\n\n\nPhone number\n\n\t\n\nEnter the phone number to which you want to send the fax. You can send multiple phone numbers in the following format:\n\n(+[country code][number])\n\n\n\n\nFiles\n\n\t\n\nAdd files you want to fax:\n\nFile name\n\nEnter the file name. For example, sample.doc\n\nData\n\nEnter the file data to the field or map the source of the file.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL to the fax files you want to attach to the message.\n\n\n\n\nHeader Text\n\n\t\n\nEnter the text that appears at the top of the fax.\n\n\n\n\nCallback URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL that can overwrite the defined URL globally.\n\n\n\n\nBatch Delay\n\n\t\n\nEnter the time in seconds for which you want to delay sending the fax. You can delay the batch up to 1 hour (3600 seconds).\n\n\n\n\nBatch collision avoidance\n\n\t\n\nSelect Yes if you want to block the fax until the receiving machine is ready or not busy:\n\nYes\n\nNo\n\nNot defined\n\n\n\n\nCancel timeout\n\n\t\n\nEnter the number of minutes after which the fax will be canceled if it has not been completed yet.\n\nEnter a value between 3 and 60.\n\n\n\n\nCaller ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Phaxio phone number which you would like to use for the caller ID.\n\nResend Fax\n\nResends a fax.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Phaxio account.\n\n\n\n\nFax ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Fax ID you want to resend.\n\nPhaxio\nConnecting Phaxio to Make\nActions\nCancel Fax\nCreate and Send Fax\nResend Fax\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

modules allow you to watch, create, update, list, and delete SMS, contacts, and groups in your MessageBird account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA MessageBird account\n\nIn order to use MessageBird with Make, Go to Make and open MessageBird module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n4. In the Connection name field, enter the name of the connection.\n\n5. In the Access Key field, enter the API key copied in step 2.\n\n6. Click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nMessages\nDelete an SMS Message\n\nDeletes an SMS message.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your MessageBird account.\n\n\n\n\nMessage ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Message ID you want to delete.\n\nRead an SMS Message\n\nGets details of an SMS message.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your MessageBird account.\n\n\n\n\nMessage ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Message ID you want to read.\n\nList SMS Messages\n\nRetrieves a list of SMS messages that were sent or received.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your MessageBird account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nEnter the number of messages Make should return during one execution cycle.\n\n\n\n\nOriginator\n\n\t\n\nEnter the sender number whose messages you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nRecipient\n\n\t\n\nEnter the recipient number whose messages you want to list.\n\n\n\n\nDirection\n\n\t\n\nSelect the message direction:\n\nSent\n\nReceived\n\n\n\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the message type:\n\nSMS\n\nBinary\n\nFlash\n\n\n\n\nStatus\n\n\t\n\nSelect the status of the messages you want to list:\n\nScheduled\n\nSent\n\nBuffered\n\nDelivered\n\nExpired\n\nDelivery Failed\n\nSend an SMS Message\n\nSends an SMS message via MessageBird.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your MessageBird account.\n\n\n\n\nRecipients\n\n\t\n\nEnter the recipient number to whom you want to send the message.\n\n\n\n\nOriginator\n\n\t\n\nEnter the sender details. Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationMastodon\nMastodon\n\nWith Mastodon modules in Make, you can:\n\ncreate, update, retrieve, and delete statuses\n\ncreate, update, and retrieve polls\n\nlist, retrieve, and delete notifications\n\ncreate, retrieve, and search accounts; retrieve an account by name or URL\n\nupload a media\n\nTo get started with Mastodon, create an account at mastodon.org.\n\nConnect Mastodon to Make\n\nTo connect Mastodon app, you need to obtain the Server Name from your Mastodon account and insert them into your Make scenario.\n\nLog in to your Make account, insert a Mastodon module in your scenario, and click the Add button next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Server Name field, enter the name of the server. For example, For example, in this URL https://uiuxdev.social/web/@devmake, uiuxdev.social is the server's name.\n\nClick Save.\n\nClick Authorize to allow Make access to your account.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Mastodon modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nConnect Mastodon with Make Using OAuth Credentials\n\nTo connect Mastodon with the Make with the OAuth credentials:\n\nLog in to your Mastodon account.\n\nClick Preferences.\n\nClick Development > New application.\n\nEnter the application name, application website, redirect URI, and select the scopes you want to allow. management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationLINE\nLINE\n\nThe Line modules enable you to monitor, publish or update posts, photos and videos in your Line account.\n\nGetting Started with Line\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Line app installed\n\nA developer account in the LINE Developers console\n\nCreated a dedicated Messaging API channel for your bot\n\nCaution\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Line to Make\n\nTo connect your Line account to Make follow these steps:\n\n1. Log in to the LINE Developers console.\n\n2. Create a new provider.\n\n3. Click the Create a Messaging API channel.\n\n4. Provide the required information and click Create to create a channel.\n\n5. In the channel created above, open the Messaging API tab and scan the QR code using your LINE app to add the channel as a friend.\n\n6. In the Messaging API tab, scroll down to the Channel access token section and click the Issue button () to generate the Channel Access Token.\n\n7. Navigate to the Basic settings tab, scroll down and copy the provided User ID.\n\n8. Go to Make and open the LINE module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n9. Enter the Channel access token you have generated in step 6 and the User ID copied in step 7 to respective fields and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nMessage\nWatch Events\n\nTriggers when an event occurs.\n\nThe webhook URL needs to be generated in Make and then added to LINE's developer settings.\n\n1. Add the Watch New Activity module to your Make scenario.\n\n2. Generate and copy the webhook URL.\n\n3. Log in to your LINE Developers account.\n\n4. Navigate to Providers > {your provider} > {your messaging API channel} > Messaging API tab.\n\n5. Enter the webhook URL copied in step 2 above to the Webhook URL field and click Update.\n\n6. Activate the Use webhook option.\n\nNow, every time an event occurs, the Watch Events module in your Make scenario is triggered.\n\nSend a Reply Message\n\nSends a reply message in a response to an event from user, group, or room.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LINE account.\n\n\n\n\nReply Token\n\n\t\n\nMap the reply token from the Watch Events module.\n\nBecause the reply token becomes invalid after a certain period of time, responses should be sent as soon as a message is received. Reply tokens can only be used once.\n\n\n\n\nMessages\n\n\t\n\nSet the messages you want to send as reply. Max 5 messages.\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the type of the message:\n\n\n\n\nText\n\n\t\n\nText\n\n\t\n\nEnter the message text. You can include the following emoji:\n\nUnicode emoji\n\nLINE emoji (Use a $ character as a placeholder and specify details in the emojis property)\n\nMax character limit: 5000\n\n\n\n\nLINE Emojis\n\n\t\n\nAdd one or more LINE emoji.\n\nThe number of emoji items must be equal to the number of $ in the Text field above.\n\nProduct ID for a set of LINE emojis. See Sendable LINE emoji list.\n\nEmoji ID for a LINE emoji inside a set. See Sendable LINE emoji list.\n\n\n\n\nSticker\n\n\t\n\nPackage ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Package ID for a set of stickers. For information on package IDs, see the Sticker list.\n\n\n\n\nSticker ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Sticker ID. For a list of sticker IDs for stickers that can be sent with the Messaging API, see the Sticker list.\n\n\n\n\nImage\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the image URL (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPG, JPEG, or PNG Max image size: No limits Max file size: 10 MB\n\n\n\n\nPreview Image URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the preview image URL (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPG, JPEG or PNG Max image size: No limits Max file size: 1 MB\n\n\n\n\nVideo\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nURL of the video file (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later mp4 Max file size: 200 MB A very wide or tall video may be cropped when played in some environments.\n\n\n\n\nPreview Image URL\n\n\t\n\nURL of the preview image (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPEG or PNG Max file size: 1 MB\n\n\n\n\nAudio\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL of the audio file (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later m4a Max file size: 200 MB Note: Only M4A files are supported on the Messaging API. If a service only supports MP3 files, you can use a service like FFmpeg to convert the files to M4A.\n\n\n\n\nDuration\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the length of the audio file (milliseconds)\n\n\n\n\nLocation\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title, address, latitude and longitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nImage Map\n\n\t\n\nImagemap messages are messages configured with an image that has multiple tappable areas. You can assign one tappable area for the entire image or different tappable areas on divided areas of the image.\n\nFor more details please refer to the LINE documentation.\n\n\n\n\nTemplate\n\n\t\n\nTemplate messages are messages with predefined layouts that you can customize. For more information, see Template messages.\n\nFor more details please refer to the LINE documentation.\n\n\n\n\nNotification Disabled\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to disable a push notification to the user when the message is sent.\n\nSend a Push Message\n\nSends a push message to a user, group, or room at any time.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LINE account.\n\n\n\n\nTo\n\n\t\n\nMap the ID of the target recipient. Use a User ID, Group ID, or Room ID returned in the Watch Eventsmodule.\n\n\n\n\nMessages\n\n\t\n\nSet the messages you want to send. Max 5 messages.\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the type of the message:\n\n\n\n\nText\n\n\t\n\nText\n\n\t\n\nEnter the message text. You can include the following emoji:\n\nUnicode emoji\n\nLINE emoji (Use a $ character as a placeholder and specify details in the emojis property)\n\nMax character limit: 5000\n\n\n\n\nLINE Emojis\n\n\t\n\nAdd one or more LINE emoji.\n\nThe number of emoji items must be equal to the number of $ in the Text field above.\n\nProduct ID for a set of LINE emojis. See Sendable LINE emoji list.\n\nEmoji ID for a LINE emoji inside a set. See Sendable LINE emoji list.\n\n\n\n\nSticker\n\n\t\n\nPackage ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Package ID for a set of stickers. For information on package IDs, see the Sticker list.\n\n\n\n\nSticker ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Sticker ID. For a list of sticker IDs for stickers that can be sent with the Messaging API, see the Sticker list.\n\n\n\n\nImage\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the image URL (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPG, JPEG, or PNG Max image size: No limits Max file size: 10 MB\n\n\n\n\nPreview Image URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the preview image URL (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPG, JPEG or PNG Max image size: No limits Max file size: 1 MB\n\n\n\n\nVideo\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nURL of the video file (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later mp4 Max file size: 200 MB A very wide or tall video may be cropped when played in some environments.\n\n\n\n\nPreview Image URL\n\n\t\n\nURL of the preview image (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later JPEG or PNG Max file size: 1 MB\n\n\n\n\nAudio\n\n\t\n\nOriginal Content URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL of the audio file (Max character limit: 1000) HTTPS over TLS 1.2 or later m4a Max file size: 200 MB Note: Only M4A files are supported on the Messaging API. If a service only supports MP3 files, you can use a service like FFmpeg to convert the files to M4A.\n\n\n\n\nDuration\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the length of the audio file (milliseconds)\n\n\n\n\nLocation\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title, address, latitude and longitude of the location.\n\n\n\n\nImage Map\n\n\t\n\nImagemap messages are messages configured with an image that has multiple tappable areas. To invite a bot, make sure that the Allow bot to join group chats option is enabled in your bot channel settings.\n\nThis includes user IDs of users who have not added the LINE Official Account as a friend or have blocked the LINE Official Account.\n\nThis feature is available only for verified or premium accounts. For more information about account types, see the Account Types of LINE Official Account page on LINE for Business.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LINE account.\n\n\n\n\nChoose\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to retrieve members from the group or room.\n\n\n\n\nGroup ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the group ID of the group you want to retrieve members from. You can retrieve the group ID using the Watch Events module (triggers when a user joins a group/room).\n\n\n\n\nRoom ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the room ID of the room you want to retrieve members from. You can retrieve the room ID using the Watch Events module (triggers when a user joins a group/room).\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of members Make will return during one scenario execution.\n\nGet a Group/Room Member Profile\n\nRetrieves a display name and profile image URL of the group/room member.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LINE account.\n\n\n\n\nChoose\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to retrieve member information from the group or room.\n\n\n\n\nRoom ID/Group ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the group ID or Room ID of the group/room you want to retrieve member information from. Max 14 characters.\n\n\n\n\nSet the Rich Menu by Default\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to display the rich menu by default.\n\n\n\n\nSource File\n\n\t\n\nMap the file you want to upload from the previous module (e.g. HTTP > Get a File or Google Drive > Download a File), or enter the file name and file data manually.\n\nImage format: JPEG or PNG\n\nImage width size (pixels): 800 to 2500\n\nImage height size (pixels): 250 or more\n\nImage aspect ratio (width/height): 1.45 or more\n\nMax file size: 1 MB\n\n\n\n\nSelect Size of Rich Menu\n\n\t\n\nSelect the size of the rich menu.\n\nLarge Size - 2500 x 1686\n\nSmall Size - 2500 x 843\n\n\n\n\nAreas\n\n\t\n\nDefine the coordinates and size of tappable areas. Required for quick reply buttons. Optional for the other message types. Max character limit: 300\n\n\n\n\nLabel\n\n\t\n\nEnter the label for the action\n\nRequired for templates other than image carousel. Max character limit: 20\n\nOptional for image carousel templates. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nEXAMPLE OF USE - LIST RICH MENUS\n\nThe following API call returns all rich menus in your LINE account:\n\nURL:\n\n/v2/bot/richmenu/list\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nThe result can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > richmenus.\n\nIn our example, 8 rich menus were returned:\n\nLINE\nGetting Started with Line\nConnecting Line to Make\nMessage\nWatch Events\nSend a Reply Message\nSend a Push Message\nSend a Broadcast Message\nDownload a Message Attachment\nNotify API\nSend a Notification\nGroup/Room\nList Group/Room Members\nGet a Group/Room Member Profile\nLeave Group/Room\nRich Menu\nList Rich Menus\nGet a Rich Menu\nCreate a Rich Menu\nDownload a Rich Menu Image\nGet a Number of Followers\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationLiveChat\nLiveChat\n\nWith LiveChat modules in Make, you can watch incoming chats and when chats are deactivated, watch users added or removed from chats, watch when threads are tagged or untagged in your LiveChat account.\n\nTo use the LiveChat modules, you must have a LiveChat account. You can create an account at accounts.livechat.com/.\n\nRefer to the LiveChat API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nGetting Started with LiveChat\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA LiveChat account - create an account at accounts.livechat.com/.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting LiveChat to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nCreate a custom application in LiveChat.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nCreate a Custom Application in LiveChat\n\nTo create a LiveChat custom application and retrieve your client credentials:\n\nGo to https://developers.livechat.com/ and log in with your LiveChat credentials.\n\nClick Build App.\n\nFill in an App name.\n\nFor Product, choose LiveChat.\n\nChoose your Infrastructure. You must choose Repository to use Deployment as well.\n\nChoose your hosting service for Repository and, if necessary, for your deployment service.\n\nClick Create App.\n\nWithin the app, in the left navigation, click App Authorization.\n\nCopy your Client ID and Client Secret values and store them in a safe place.\n\nAdd the following for Redirect URI whitelist: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/app\n\nFor Access scopes, add the scopes you will need. The following scopes should cover any needs you may have, though your use may vary.\n\nYou will use these values in the <Client ID > and <Client Secret > fields in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with LiveChat in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a LiveChat module to your scenario, and click Create a webhook.\n\nOptional: Enter a name for the webhook in the Webhook name field.\n\nClick Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, center the values copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more LiveChat modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nChats\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in LiveChat once you add an instant trigger to your scenario.\n\nWatch Incoming Chat\nWatch Chat Deactivated\nChat Users\n\nMake automatically creates a webhook in LiveChat once you add an instant trigger to your scenario.\n\nWatch User Added to the Chat\nWatch User Removed from a Chat\nOthers\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Webhooks\nLiveChat\nGetting Started with LiveChat\nConnecting LiveChat to Make\nCreate a Custom Application in LiveChat\nEstablish the connection with LiveChat in Make\nChats\nWatch Incoming Chat\nWatch Chat Deactivated\nChat Users\nWatch User Added to the Chat\nWatch User Removed from a Chat\nOthers\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

mailparser.io account. Add the Watch Email Parsed module to your Make scenario.\n\n2. Generate and copy the webhook URL.\n\n3. Log in to your mailparser.io account.\n\n4. Navigate to the desired Inbox > Integrations > Add New Integrations button.\n\n5. Select the Generic Webhook option.\n\n6. Enter the webhook name and the Webhook URL you have copied in step 2 above in the Target URL field. Enter advanced options, if needed, and click SAVE & TEST.\n\nNow, every time an email is parsed in your mailparser.io account, the Watch Email Parsed module in your Make scenario is triggered.\n\nmailparser.io\nGetting Started with mailparser.io\nConnecting mailparser.io to Make\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationJIRA Cloud Platform\nJIRA Cloud Platform\n\nWith JIRA Cloud Platform modules in Make, you can watch, create, update, retrieve, search, list, assign/unassign, and delete issues, issue comments, issue links, watchers, custom field options, components, project visions, and users and make API calls.\n\nTo get started with JIRA Cloud Platform, create a JIRA account at atlassian.com.\n\nNote\n\nRefer to the JIRA Cloud Platform API documentation for the list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect JIRA Cloud Platform to Make\n\nTo connect JIRA Cloud Platform to Make, you must first create an API token.\n\nTo do so, follow these steps:\n\nGo to https://id.atlassian.com/manage/api-tokens and log in.\n\nClick Create API token.\n\nEnter a Label for the API token and click Create.\n\nClick Copy and store your generated token in a safe place as you will not be able to view the token again after closing this dialog.\n\nLog in to your Make account and add a JIRA Cloud Platform module to a scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nFill in the Service URL and Username and paste your API Token from step 4.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more JIRA Cloud Platform modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nSet up JIRA Cloud Platform Webhooks\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. Follow the steps below to set them up.\n\nNote\n\nYour JIRA account must have Administer Jira: Global permissions to create webhooks.\n\nGo to your Make account and open the JIRA Cloud Platform Watch Issues Instant Acid module in a scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Webhook field.\n\nOptional: In the Webhook name field, enter a name for the webhook.\n\nSelect the Hook type and click Save.\n\nCopy the generated URL address and click OK.\n\nGo to Jira and click the Settings Icon > System. In the Advanced section, click WebHooks.\n\nHere you can create a webhook using the copied URL from step 5. Please refer to the Jira Cloud platform Webhooks documentation as a guide.\n\nCaution\n\nFrom July 1, 2023, there will be a limit of up to 100 active Jira admin webhooks per Jira instance.\n\nBuild JIRA Cloud Platform Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nWatch Issues\n\nTriggers when a ticket event occurs.\n\nWatch Issues\n\nTriggers when an issue is created or updated.\n\nCreate an Issue\n\nCreates a new issue.\n\nUpdate an Issue\n\nUpdates an existing issue.\n\nGet an Issue\n\nReturns the details for an issue.\n\nSearch Issues\n\nSearches for issues.\n\nList Current Available Transitions in an Issue\n\nLists current available transitions in an issue.\n\nUpdate an Issue Status (Transition Issue)\n\nUpdates an issue status.\n\nAssign/Unassign an Issue\n\nAssigns an issue to a user.\n\nGet Changelog of an Issue\n\nRetrieves changelog of an issue.\n\nDelete an Issue\n\nDeletes an issue.\n\nAdd an Issue Comment\n\nAdds a comment to an issue.\n\nUpdate an Issue Comment\n\nUpdates a comment to a specific issue.\n\nGet an Issue Comment\n\nReturns an issue comment.\n\nList Issue Comments\n\nReturns all comments for an issue.\n\nDelete an Issue Comment\n\nDeletes a comment on a specific issue.\n\nCreate an Issue Link\n\nCreates an issue link.\n\nDelete an Issue Link\n\nDeletes an issue link.\n\nAdd a Watcher\n\nAdds a user as a watcher on an issue.\n\nList Issue Watchers\n\nReturns the watchers for an issue.\n\nDelete a Watcher from an Issue\n\nDeletes a user as a watcher of an issue.\n\nAdd an Attachment\n\nAdds a new attachment to a ticket.\n\nDownload an Attachment\n\nDownloads an attachment.\n\nDelete an Attachment\n\nDeletes an attachment.\n\nCreate Custom Fields Options\n\nCreates options for a custom select field.\n\nUpdate Custom Fields Options\n\nUpdates the options of a custom field.\n\nGet All Custom Field Options\n\nReturns a list of all the options of a select list issue field.\n\nReorder Custom Fields Options\n\nChanges the order of custom field options or cascading options in a context.\n\nDelete Custom Field Option\n\nDeletes a custom field option.\n\nCreate a Component\n\nCreates a component.\n\nUpdate a Component\n\nUpdates a component.\n\nList Project Components\n\nRetrieves project components.\n\nDelete a Component\n\nDeletes a component.\n\nCreate a Project Version\n\nCreates a project version.\n\nUpdate a Project Version\n\nUpdates a project version.\n\nList Project Versions\n\nRetrieves all versions in a project.\n\nDelete a Project Version\n\nDeletes a project version.\n\nList Users\n\nRetrieves all users (active and inactive).\n\nSearch Users\n\nSearches for users by query.\n\nGet a User\n\nReturns a user.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nCustom fields\n\nWhen retrieving issues from JIRA via webhooks or Get Actions, basic sample data from the general JIRA installation is available. In order to get your custom fields, there must be at least one issue available in JIRA for Make to retrieve it and remember the custom fields. Once you run your scenario (or run a single JIRA module) the fields become available. These custom fields are available only on your computer as they are saved in your browser. If you access Make from another computer, you must repeat the process.\n\nJIRA Cloud Platform\nConnect JIRA Cloud Platform to Make\nSet up JIRA Cloud Platform Webhooks\nBuild JIRA Cloud Platform Scenarios\nCustom fields\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationInfobip\nInfobip\n\nThe Infobip modules allow you to send and retrieve the SMS in your Infobip account.\n\nGetting Started with Infobip\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAn Infobipe account - create an account at infobip.com/.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Infobip to Make\n\nTo connect your Infobip account to Make you need to obtain the Email address and API Key from your Infobip account and insert them in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your Infobip account.\n\n2. From the Dashboard, copy the API Key to your clipboard.\n\n3. Log in to your Make account and add a scenario from Infobip app into an Make scenario.\n\n4. Click Add next to the Connection field.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n6. In the API Key field, enter the API key copied in step 2.\n\n7. In the Domain field, enter your Infobip account domain name. For example, if your account URL address is https://xyz.infobip.com, then your domain is xyz.\n\n8. Click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\nWatch SMS\n\nTriggers when a new SMS is sent.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Infobip account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of SMS Make should receive during one execution cycle.\n\nActions\nSend an SMS\n\nSends an SMS message.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Infobip account.\n\n\n\n\nMessages\n\n\t\n\nAdd the messages you want to send:\n\nDestination\n\n\t\n\nAdd the details of the recipient to send the message:ToEnter (map) the recipient's email address.Message IDEnter (map) the Message-ID you want to send to the recipient.\n\n\n\n\nText\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the message text you want to send.\n\n\n\n\nTransliteration\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the transliteration of your sent message from one script to another.Transliteration is used to replace characters that are not recognized as part of your defaulted alphabet.\n\n\n\n\nIntermediate Report\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to send the message immediately.\n\n\n\n\nFlash\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to send hte message as a flash to the recipient that displays on the lock screen.\n\n\n\n\nValidity Report\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the message validity in minutes.\n\n\n\n\nFrom\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the sender details who is sending the message. You can enter a maximum of three characters.\n\n\n\n\nSend At\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the date and time when you want to send the message. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\n\n\n\nLanguage Code\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the language in which the message is to be sent:\n\nTurkish\n\nGreek\n\nCyrillic\n\nCentral European\n\nNon-Unicode\n\n\n\n\nNotify URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the URL on your call back server to which a delivery report will be sent. For more information, see the Delivery report format.\n\n\n\n\nNotify Content-Type\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the preferred content type for the notification:\n\nJSON\n\nXML\n\n\n\n\nNotify\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to receive the notification for the message.\n\n\n\n\nCallback Data\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the additional client's data that will be sent on the Notify URL.\n\n\n\n\nBinary\n\n\t\n\nAdd the binary items such as ESM class, Hex, and Data Coding details for the message.\n\n\n\n\nDelivery Time Window\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the specific scheduling options to send a message within daily or hourly intervals. For example, Monday, Tuesday, etc.,\n\n\n\n\nTo\n\n\t\n\nHourEnter (map) the Hour the time window opens when used in from property or closes when used into the property.MinuteEnter (map) the minute the time window opens when used in from property or closes when used into the property.\n\n\n\n\nFrom\n\n\t\n\nHourEnter (map) the hour the time window opens when used in from property or closes when used into the property.MinuteEnter (map) the minute the time window opens when used in from property or closes when used into the property.\n\n\n\n\nRegional\n\n\t\n\nAdd the regional distributor ledger technology (DLT) information:Content Template IDEnter (map) the Registered DTL Content Template ID that matches the message you are sending.Principal Entity IDEnter (map) your assigned DTL Principal Entity ID.\n\n\n\n\nBulk ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Bulk ID assigned to the request if you are messaging multiple recipients or sending multiple messages via a single API request. If not provided, it will be auto-generated and returned in the API response. This Bulk ID is used to fetch delivery reports and message logs.\n\n\n\n\nTracking\n\n\t\n\nAdd the tracking details:\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the tracking type. For example, one-time PIN or social invites.\n\n\n\n\nTrack\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the option to track the message for conversion rates:\n\nSMS\n\nURL\n\n\n\n\nProcess Key\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the process key which identifies the conversion tracking.\n\n\n\n\nSending Speed Limit\n\n\t\n\nAdd the SMS send limit:AmountEnter (map) the number of messages to send per time unit.Note: Boosting this parameter will not result in faster sending speeds beyond infrastructure capabilities.Time UnitSelect or map the time unit to send the SMS:\n\nDay\n\nHour\n\nMinute\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Infobip account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://<domain>.api.infobip.com For example,/people/2/tagsFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Infobip API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST to create a new entry.\n\nPUT to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH to make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE to delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - Get Tags\n\nThe following API call returns all the tags from your Infobip account:\n\nURL: /people/2/tags\n\nMethod: GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > tags. In our example, 3 tags were returned:\n\nInfobip\nGetting Started with Infobip\nConnecting Infobip to Make\nTriggers\nWatch SMS\nActions\nSend an SMS\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Tags\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

update, retrieve and delete the contacts in your Global SMS account.\n\nTo get started with the Global SMS, create an account at smsglobal.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnect Global SMS with Make\n\nTo connect the Global SMS app with the  Make:\n\nLog in to your Global SMS account.\n\nClick Account Information > API.\n\nCopy the API Key to a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make and add a module from the Global SMS into a  Make scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Connection field.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the details copied in step 3 and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully connected the Global SMS app with  Make and can now build scenarios.\n\nActions\n\nYou can get the account balance of the logged-in user and send SMS using the following modules.\n\nSend SMS To Recipients\n\nSends an SMS message to a single recipient or multiple recipients.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Global SMS account.\n\n\n\n\nSMS Originator\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the number your recipients see as the sender.\n\nNote\n\nThey may reply to that number. Mobile and landline numbers should be verified on the Send SMS screen in the Global SMS app\n\n\n\n\nDestinations\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the recipient's mobile numbers including the country code. For example, 0501122337.\n\n\n\n\nMessage\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the text message to send. The message must be between 1 and 1005 characters long.\n\nGet Balance\n\nGet your account's balance.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Global SMS account.\n\nGlobal SMS\nConnect Global SMS with Make\nActions\nSend SMS To Recipients\nGet Balance\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationGmail\nGmail \n\nWith Gmail modules in Make, you can manage the emails, email labels, and attachments in your Gmail account.\n\nTo use the Gmail modules, you must have a Gmail account. You can create an account at myaccount.google.com.\n\nRefer to the Gmail API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nNote\n\nMake's use and transfer of information received from Google APIs to any other app will adhere to Google API Services User Data Policy.\n\nConnect Gmail to Make\nImportant\n\nIf you want to connect an email that ends with @gmail or @googlemail, you must create a custom OAuth client in Google Cloud Console and get your project client credentials to establish the connection in Make.\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Gmail module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional for Gmail users with non-@gmail or @googlemail domains: Switch on the Show advanced settings toggle and enter your Google Cloud Console project client credentials. For more information, see the Create and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Gmail section below.\n\nClick Sign in with Google.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Gmail modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Gmail\n\nTo connect to Make using your own client credentials, you can create and configure a project in the Google Cloud Console.\n\nImportant\n\nThis is required for emails that end with @gmail or @googlemail.\n\nCreate a Google Cloud Console project for Gmail\n\nTo create a Google Cloud Console project:\n\nLog in to the Google Cloud Console using your Google credentials.\n\nIn the top menu, click Select a project > New project.\n\nEnter a Project name and select the Location for your project.\n\nClick Create.\n\nIn the top menu, check if your new project is selected in the Select a project dropdown. If not, select the project you just created.\n\nEnable APIs for Gmail\n\nTo enable the required APIs:\n\nOpen the left navigation menu and go to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch for and enable the following API: Gmail API\n\nConfigure your OAuth consent screen for Gmail\n\nTo configure your OAuth consent screen:\n\nGo to APIs & Services > OAuth consent screen.\n\nUnder User Type, select External.\n\nFor more information regarding user types, refer to Google's Exceptions to verification requirements documentation.\n\nClick Create.\n\nFill in the required fields with your information.\n\nIn the Authorized domains section, add make.com and integromat.com.\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nIn the Scopes page, click Add or remove scopes, add the following scopes, and click Update: https://mail.google.com/\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nOptional: If your project will remain in the Testing publishing status, add test user emails on the Test users page, then click Save and continue.\n\nCreate your Gmail client credentials\n\nTo create your client credentials:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Credentials.\n\nClick + Create Credentials > OAuth client ID.\n\nIn the Application type dropdown, select Web application.\n\nUpdate the Name of your OAuth client. This will help you identify it in the console.\n\nIn the Authorized redirect URIs section, click + Add URI and enter the following redirect URI:\n\nhttps://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/google-restricted\n\nClick Create.\n\nCopy your Client ID and Client secret values and store them in a safe place.\n\nYou will use these values in the Client ID and Client Secret fields in Make.\n\nBuild Gmail Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTriggers\nWatch Emails\nActions\nCopy an Email\nCreate a Draft\nDelete an Email\nMark an Email as Read\nMark an Email as Unread\nModify Email Labels\nMove an Email\nSend an Email\nIterators\nIterate Attachments\nCommon Problems\n\nHere you can find solutions for the most common issues when working with Gmail in Make.\n\nError 400: Failed to Verify a Connection\n\nYour connection has expired and is no longer valid. You need to reauthorizae the connection every seven days. Refer to Google OAuth documentation for more information.\n\nTo avoid reauthorization every seven days, publish your project in Google Cloud Console:\n\nLog in to the Google Cloud Console using your Google credentials.\n\nGo to APIs & Service > OAuth consent screen.\n\nUnder Publishing status, click Publish app.\n\nNote\n\nIf the Needs verification message appears, choose whether to go through the Google verification process for the app or to connect to your unverified app. Currently connecting to unverified apps works in Make, but we cannot guarantee the Google will allow connections to unverified apps for an indefinite period.\n\nError 403: Access Denied\n\nYou didn't add a test user for your project in Google Cloud Console, and the project has the Testing status. You need to add the email address associated with the Google account you want to connect with Make as a Test user.\n\nLog in to the Google Cloud Console using your Google credentials.\n\nGo to APIs & Services > OAuth consent screen.\n\nUnder Test users, + Add Users and enter an email of a user that you want to create a connection for.\n\nClick Save.\n\nError 403: Access Not Configured\n\nThe Gmail API was disabled in the Google Cloud Console. You need to enable it again.\n\nGmail\nConnect Gmail to Make\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Gmail\nBuild Gmail Scenarios\nTriggers\nActions\nIterators\nCommon Problems\nError 400: Failed to Verify a Connection\nError 403: Access Denied\nError 403: Access Not Configured\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationGoogle Meet\nGoogle Meet\n\nWith Google Meet modules in Make, you can create meetings in your Google Meet account.\n\nTo get started with Google Meet, create an account at accounts.google.com.\n\nNote\n\nMake's use and transfer of information received from Google APIs to any other app will adhere to Google API Services User Data Policy.\n\nConnect Google Meet to Make\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Google Meet module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nClick the Sign in with Google button and select your Google account.\n\nReview the access information and click Allow.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Google Meet modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nActions\nCreate a Meeting\n\nCreates a new Google Meet in a specified calendar.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Google Meet account.\n\n\n\n\nCalendar ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the Calendar ID in which you want to create the meeting.\n\n\n\n\nColor\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the applicable color for the event.\n\n\n\n\nEvent Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the event name.\n\n\n\n\nAll Day Event\n\n\t\n\nSelect the checkbox if the event is scheduled for the entire day.\n\n\n\n\nStart Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the start date of the event. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\n\n\n\nEnd Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the end date of the event. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\n\n\n\nSend Notifications about the event creation\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the options to send the notifications about the event:\n\nTo All Guests\n\nTo non-Google Calendar Events\n\nTo None\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the event details.\n\n\n\n\nLocation\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the location details of the event. For example, a conference room or an online meeting link.\n\n\n\n\nUse the Default reminder settings for this event\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to use the default reminder setting for the event.\n\n\n\n\nReminders\n\n\t\n\nAdd the reminders for the event:\n\nMethod - Select or map the reminder method. For example, Email.\n\nMinutes - Enter the minutes before the meeting to send the reminder. For example, 10 to send the reminder before 10 minutes to the meeting.\n\n\n\n\nAttendees\n\n\t\n\nAdd the attendees:\n\nName - Enter (map) the attendee's name.\n\nEmail - Enter (map) the attendee's email address.\n\n\n\n\nShow me as\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the option to display your status when you are in the event:\n\nBusy\n\nAvailable\n\n\n\n\nVisibility\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the event visibility:\n\nDefault\n\nPrivate\n\nPublic\n\n\n\n\nGuests can modify the event\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to allow the guests to modify the event. For example, updating the date of the event.\n\n\n\n\nRecurrence\n\n\t\n\nAdd the recurrence of the event. Enter a list of RRULE, EXRULE, RDATE, and EXDATE lines for a recurring event, as specified in RFC5545. For example,RRULE:FREQ=WEEKLY;UNTIL=20250701T170000Z\n\nFor more information on the Google Meet events, see the related API Documentation.\n\nGoogle Meet\nConnect Google Meet to Make\nActions\nCreate a Meeting\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

to your Google account. Click your organization and select NEW PROJECT.\n\nEnter a name for the project, select your organization, and browse the project location. Click CREATE.\n\nSelect the project created and click IAM & Admin.\n\nClick Service Accounts.\n\nClick CREATE SERVICE ACCOUNT.\n\nEnter the service account details and click CREATE AND CONTINUE. You can grant optional access and click DONE.\n\nSelect the newly created service account and click the three dots. Click Manage keys.\n\nClick KEYS > ADD KEY.\n\nSelect the Key type and click CREATE.\n\nCopy the Client Email and Private Key from the downloaded key.\n\nConnect Google Chat to Make\n\nTo connect Google Chat app, you need to obtain the Client Email and Private Key details from your Google account.\n\nIn your Make account, insert a Google Chat module in your scenario and click the Add button next to the Connection field.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Client Email and Private Key fields, enter the details obtained above and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Google Chat modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nGoogle Chat\nGet Client Email and Private Key\nConnect Google Chat to Make\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationDiscord\nDiscord\n\nThe Discord modules allow you to create, update, list, and/or delete channels, channel messages, reactions, and webhooks in your Discord account.\n\nTo get started with Discord, create an account at https://discordapp.com/register.\n\nNote\n\nAccording to Discord, message content will be categorized as Privileged Intent starting September 1, 2022.\n\nThis means that users who have installed our verified bot on their Discord server will not be able to use the following Make modules with the bot:\n\nWatch Channel Messages\n\nList Channel Messages\n\nGet a Message\n\nUsers who installed the Make verified bot to connect to the Discord app on our platform will see the empty values of messages that the channel member sends for the fields, content, embeds, attachments, and components in the output.\n\nThe Make verified bot is still able to receive the messages for the above modules under the following conditions:\n\nMessages the bot sends\n\nMessages the bot receives in DMs\n\nMessages in which the bot is mentioned\n\nIf you want to use the aforementioned modules, you can create a custom connection using a separate client ID.\n\nConnect Discord to Make\n\nYou can connect the Discord app to Make in two ways:\n\nConnect using OAuth2\n\nConnect using OAuth2 and using your own app credentials\n\nConnect Discord to Make using OAuth2\n\nTo connect your Discord account to Make, you need to create a server and channels.\n\nLogin to your Discord account and create a server.\n\nEnter the details of the server and click Create.\n\nGo to Make and open the Discord module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nSelect the server created in step 1, allow the permissions for messages and channels, and click Authorize.\n\nYou have successfully connected the Discord app and can now build scenarios.\n\n.\n\nConnect to Discord using OAuth2 and your own credentials\n\nTo connect to Discord, you need to create a developer account to obtain the bot token, client ID, and client secret values by creating a custom application from your Discord developer account.\n\nLog in to the Discord developer account.\n\nClick Create New Application, enter a name for the application, and click Create.\n\nOn the left menu, click OAuth2, add the following redirect URIs, and click Save Changes.\n\nhttps://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/discord\n\nhttps://www.make.com/oauth/cb/discord\n\nNote\n\nEnable Message Content Intent in your app settings if you want to receive the full message content.\n\nIn the Client Information section, copy the CLIENT ID value to a safe place. In the CLIENT SECRET field, click Reset secret, accept the warning, and copy the secret value to a safe place.\n\nNote\n\nEvery time you reset the token, the existing connections will stop working. You need to reauthenticate the connection with this new token.\n\nOn the left menu, click Bot > Add bot.\n\nOptional: Change the default name of the bot.\n\nOptional: Enable the Privileged Gateway Intent settings if you want to receive full message content from all the modules.\n\nClick Reset to generate the bot token, accept the alert, and copy the bot token to a safe place as you can see the token only once.\n\nNote\n\nEvery time you reset the token, the existing connections will stop working. You need to reauthenticate the connection with this new token.\n\nLog in to your Make, add a module from the Discord app, click Add next to the Connection field, and click Show Advanced Settings.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Bot Token field, enter the token copied in step 7.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the values copied in step 4 in the respective fields, select the bot permissions, and click Save.\n\nSelect the server to which you connect.\n\nConfirm the access by clicking Authorise.\n\nYou have successfully the Discord bot to Make and can now access messages content.\n\nMessages\nChannels\nReactions\nMember\nEvent\n\nYou can create, update, list, retrieve, and delete guild events with the following modules.\n\nList Guild Events\nGet a Guild Event\nCreate a Guild Event\nUpdate a Guild Event\nDelete a Guild Event\nWebhooks\n\nYou can create, send messages, and delete webhook bots with the following modules.\n\nCreate a Webhook Bot\nSend a Message by Webhook Bot\nDelete a Webhook Bot\nOther\n\nYou can update current bots and call APIs with the following modules.\n\nUpdate a Current Bot\nMake an API Call\nDiscord\nConnect Discord to Make\nConnect Discord to Make using OAuth2\nConnect to Discord using OAuth2 and your own credentials\nMessages\nWatch Channel Messages\nList Channel Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationFireText\nFireText\n\nThe FireText modules allow you to create, update, list, and delete the contacts, and messages in your FireText account.\n\nGetting Started with FireText\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA FireText account - create an account at app.firetext.co.uk/signup.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting FireText to Make\n\nTo connect your FireText account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your FireText account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your FireText account.\n\nClick Settings () Icon > API.\n\nCopy the API Key to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the FireText module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection and select the Authorization Type:\n\nEmail and Password\n\nAPI Key\n\nIf you have selected the Authorization Type as Email and Password, enter your FireText account credentials and click Continue.\n\n(OR)\n\nIf you have selected the Authorization Type as API Key, enter the API key copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nContacts\nCreate a Contact\n\nCreates a new contact.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nMobile Telephone\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's phone number. Remove the + sign and any leading zeros when using international codes. A UK number can start 07 or 447.\n\n\n\n\nFirst Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's first name.\n\n\n\n\nLast Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's last name.\n\n\n\n\nGroup ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Group ID to which you add the contact. You can choose to add this contact to a pre-defined group. Within FireText, click Contacts > Edit on your chosen group. The API ID is set here for your group within the Advanced Options section.\n\n\n\n\nSub-Account ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect a sub-account ID for the contact. Add the contact to a specified sub-account.Sub-account is set to UK numbers as default.Contact hello@firetext.co.uk if you need to switch to International numbers.\n\n\n\n\nCustom Field (1 - 3)\n\n\t\n\nAdd any custom field for the contact. For example, Address.\n\nGet a Contact\n\nRetrieves the stored contact information for a given mobile number in your account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nMobile Telephone\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's phone number whose details you want to retrieve. Remove the + sign and any leading zeros when using international codes. A UK number can start 07 or 447.\n\n\n\n\nSub-Account ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect a sub-account ID for the contact. Add the contact to a specified sub-account.Sub-account is set to UK numbers as default.Contact hello@firetext.co.uk if you need to switch to International numbers.\n\nUpdate a Contact\n\nUpdates an existing contact specified by mobile telephone number.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nMobile Telephone\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's phone number whose details you want to update. Remove the + sign and any leading zeros when using international codes. A UK number can start 07 or 447.\n\n\n\n\nFirst Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's first name.\n\n\n\n\nLast Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the contact's last name.\n\n\n\n\nGroup ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Group ID to which you add the contact. You can choose to add this contact to a pre-defined group. Within FireText, click Contacts > Edit on your chosen group. The API ID is set here for your group within the Advanced Options section.\n\n\n\n\nSub-Account ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect a sub-account ID for the contact. Add the contact to a specified sub-account.Sub-account is set to UK numbers as default.Contact hello@firetext.co.uk if you need to switch to International numbers.\n\n\n\n\nCustom Field (1 - 3)\n\n\t\n\nAdd any custom field for the contact. For example, Address.\n\nMessages\nWatch Message Sent\n\nTriggers when a message is sent.\n\nWebhook Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\nSee the Connecting to FireText Webhook using Make to add the webhook to your FireText account.\n\nSend a Message\n\nSends an SMS message from your FireText account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nMessage\n\n\t\n\nEnter the message text you want to send.\n\nFor GSM, a single message is 160 characters, longer messages are 153 each (2=306,3=459,4=612). Unicode is 70 characters or 66 per part for longer messages. Must be at most 612 characters long.\n\n\n\n\nFrom\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Sender ID that is displayed when the message arrives on the handset. This can be your company name or reply number. This field can only be alpha-numeric.\n\n\n\n\nTo\n\n\t\n\nEnter the recipient's telephone number. Remove the + sign and any leading zeros when using international codes. A UK number can start 07 or 447.\n\n\n\n\nGroup\n\n\t\n\nThis allows you to easily send a message to a pre-defined group within your FireText.co.uk account. Simply include the API ID specified for the group. Any duplicates or opt-outs will be ignored.\n\n\n\n\nSub-Account ID\n\n\t\n\nYour sub-account ID. Add the contact to a specified sub-account.Sub-account is set to UK numbers as default.Contact hello@firetext.co.ukif you need to switch to International numbers.\n\n\n\n\nTemplate ID\n\n\t\n\nThis allows you to choose a pre-defined template for your message content.\n\n\n\n\nSchedule\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date when the message is scheduled to send. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\n\n\n\nExpires\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date on which the message expires. See the list of supported date and time formats.\n\n\n\n\nInterval\n\n\t\n\nIf you want to specify the messages specifies the repeat interval between messages in days.\n\n\n\n\nReference\n\n\t\n\nIf set, you can record a custom ID against the message batch, which will be passed back in the delivery receipt.\n\n\n\n\nReceipt\n\n\t\n\nEnter the alternate receipt URL. Instead of using the receipt URL as defined within your FireText.co.uk account, receipts will be sent to this URL.\n\n\n\n\nUnicode\n\n\t\n\nSelect the message Unicode type:\n\nGSM Characters Only (default)\n\nAlways assume Unicode\n\nAuto-detect from the message content\n\nRemove a Scheduled Message\n\nRemoves a scheduled message specified by ID.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nMessage ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Message-ID whose schedule you want to remove.\n\n\n\n\nSub-Account ID\n\n\t\n\nYour sub-account ID. Add the contact to a specified sub-account.Sub-account is set to UK numbers as default.Contact hello@firetext.co.uk if you need to switch to International numbers.\n\nOther\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your FireText account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://www.firetext.co.uk/api/. For example: /receivedmessages\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the FireText API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - Check Credit\n\nThe following API call returns the credit balance from your FireText account:\n\nURL:\n\n/credit\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body. \n\nIn our example, the module returns the credit balance.\n\nConnecting to FireText Webhook using Make\n\nOpen any Watch module, establish a connection as mentioned in the respective modules, Click Save, and copy the URL address to your clipboard.\n\nLog in to your FireText account. Click Settings > API.\n\nBased on the messages you want to watch, in the Delivery Receipts, and/or Receiving SMS field(s), enter the webhook URL address you have copied in step 1.\n\nClick UPDATE DETAILS.\n\nThe webhook is added successfully.\n\nFireText\nGetting Started with FireText\nConnecting FireText to Make\nContacts\nCreate a Contact\nGet a Contact\nUpdate a Contact\nMessages\nWatch Message Sent\nSend a Message\nRemove a Scheduled Message\nOther\nMake an API Call\nConnecting to FireText Webhook using Make\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsProductivityNotion\nNotion\n\nWith the Notion modules in Make, you can watch, retrieve, create, append, and update databases, database items, pages, page content, search for objects, list users, and make API calls.\n\nTo use the Notion modules, you must have a Notion account. Your Notion account must have admin permissions to establish the connection in Make. You can create a Notion account at notion.so.\n\nRefer to the Notion API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Notion to Make\n\nMake provides two ways to connect the Notion app:\n\nNotion Internal connection\n\nNotion Public connection\n\nEstablish a Notion Internal Connection\n\nTo establish a Notion internal connection:\n\nLog in to your Notion account.\n\nClick Settings & Members > Connections > Develop or manage integrations from the sidebar or go to the My integrations page.\n\nClick New Integration.\n\nSelect the Associate workspace, fill in the integration Name, upload a logo (optional), choose the Associated workspace, and click Submit.\n\nGo to Capabilities, update the requested capabilities, and click Save changes.\n\nGo to Secrets, click Show next to your internal integration token, and copy the token. Store your token in a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make account and add a Notion module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nIn the Connection type dropdown, select Notion Internal.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Internal Integration Token field, paste the token copied in Step 6.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Notion modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nIf the databases are not visible in the Database ID > Search field, follow the instructions in Add Databases to be visible in Make to add them.\n\nEstablish a Notion Public Connection\n\nTo establish a Notion public connection:\n\nLog in to your Make account and add a Notion module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nIn the Connection type dropdown, select Notion Public.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional: Click Show Advanced Settings and enter your client credentials. See Obtain Notion Client Credentials.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account, click Select pages, select the pages you want Make to have access to, and click Allow access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Notion modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nObtain Notion Client Credentials\n\nTo obtain client credentials:\n\nLog in to your Notion account.\n\nClick Settings & Members > Connections > Develop or manage integrations from the sidebar or go to the My integrations page.\n\nClick New Integration.\n\nSelect the Associate workspace, fill in the integration Name, upload a logo (optional), choose the Associated workspace, and click Submit.\n\nGo to Capabilities, update the requested capabilities, and click Save changes.\n\nGo to Distribution and click the toggle to make the integration public.\n\nFill in your organization information and click Submit.\n\nRedirect URIs\n\n\t\n\nEnter the redirect URI:\n\nhttps://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/notion2\n\n\n\n\nCompany name\n\n\t\n\nName of your company or organization. You may use your own name if this does not apply.\n\n\n\n\nWebsite or homepage\n\n\t\n\nUsed to link to your integration’s website or homepage in your integration page and authentication screens.\n\n\n\n\nTagline\n\n\t\n\nOptional: A short description of the integration.\n\n\n\n\nPrivacy policy\n\n\t\n\nURL address used to link to your integration’s privacy policy in your integration page and authentication screens.\n\n\n\n\nTerms of use\n\n\t\n\nURL address used to link to your integration’s terms of use in your integration page and authentication screens.\n\n\n\n\nSupport email\n\n\t\n\nUsed to link to your integration’s support email in your integration page and authentication screens.\n\n\n\n\nNotion URL for optional template\n\n\t\n\nOptional. URL must be for a public Notion page. Use this field if you'd like to duplicate a template into a user's workspace during OAuth.\n\nClick Continue in the Switch to Public integration? prompt.\n\nCopy the OAuth client ID and OAuth client secret and save them in a safe place. You will not be able to view the OAuth client secret more than once.\n\nYou have successfully created your client credentials.\n\nAdd Databases to be visible in Make\n\nFor the Notion internal connection, by default, Notion databases do not appear in the Database ID field > Search option. You must manually add them to the Make app from your Notion account.\n\nTo add databases from your Notion account to Make app:\n\nLog in to your Notion account.\n\nEnter into the database you want to add to Make , click on ... in the top right corner, click Add connections, search for and click on the integration you previously created, and click Confirm.\n\nThe database is successfully shared and you can now see it in a module's Database ID > Search field.\n\nRetrieve added databases and pages after establishing the connection\nNote\n\nIf new databases or pages are added to the Notion account, you must revoke the connection in your Notion account and reauthorize the connection in Make to retrieve the added databases or pages.\n\nTo retrieve the newly added databases and pages:\n\nLog in to your Notion account.\n\nClick Settings & members > Connections > ... > Disconnect all users.\n\nGo to your Make account Connections page, search for your Notion connection, and click Reauthorize.\n\nYou can now see the newly added databases or pages in your Notion Make connection.\n\nBuild Notion Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nDatabase Item\n\nWatch Database Items\n\nGet a Database Item\n\nNote: Add the List Page Property Items module to retrieve the complete details of a property item if the output variable contains the has_more value. This means you must paginate to retrieve all the property item's property values in the page object as Notion imposes a 25-page reference limit.\n\nCreate a Database Item\n\nAppend a Database Item Content\n\nUpdate a Database Item\n\nDatabase/Page\n\nWatch Databases/Pages\n\nSearch Objects\n\nGet a Database\n\nGet a Page\n\nCreate a Database\n\nCreate a Page\n\nUpdate a Database\n\nUpdate a Page\n\nPage Content\n\nWatch Page Contents\n\nList Page Contents\n\nList Page Property Items\n\nNote: Can be used with the following property types: title, text, relation, and person.\n\nUse this module when a property on a database item or page output contains the has more value, indicating there are more than 25 items in that field and you much paginate to retrieve all items in that column.\n\nGet a Page Content\n\nAppend a Page Content\n\nUpdate a Page Content\n\nNote: In the Type field, select the page content type that corresponds to the Page Content ID. If an incorrect Type is selected, an error will appear. The page content type cannot be changed using this module.\n\nDelete a Page Content\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nList Users\n\nNotion\nConnect Notion to Make\nEstablish a Notion Internal Connection\nEstablish a Notion Public Connection\nObtain Notion Client Credentials\nAdd Databases to be visible in Make\nRetrieve added databases and pages after establishing the connection\nBuild Notion Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
