Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationFacebook Messenger\nFacebook Messenger\n\nWith Facebook Messenger apps in Make, you can watch and send messages, send an action, upload an attachment, or get a sender in your Facebook Messenger account.\n\nTo use the Facebook Messenger modules, you must have a Facebook Developer account. You can create an account at https://developers.facebook.com/.\n\nRefer to the Facebook API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Facebook Messenger to Make\n\nTo establish the connection with a Trigger module, you must create a webhook with a Verify Token and add this information into your app in the Facebook Developer Portal.\n\nTo establish the connection with an Action module, you must generate an Access Token in your app in the Facebook Developer Portal.\n\nThe following example, How to create a bot and connect it to Facebook Messenger and Make, describes both processes in a possible scenario.\n\nHow to create a bot and connect it to Facebook Messenger and Make\n\nThe Facebook Messenger app supports a bot's connection that can then be used to receive and send messages on behalf of a designated page that belongs to the bot.\n\nLog in to the Facebook developer portal and click Create App in the upper right corner.\n\nChoose Other as the use case for your app and click Next.\n\nAdd your App name and Contact email, then click Create app.\n\nOnce you create the app, you will be shown the Product Setup page. Select Messenger and click Set up.\n\nScroll down until you see the Configure webhooks section and click Configure. Click the Add Callback URL button. You will be prompted to fill in the Edit Callback URL and Verify Token fields. The required values can be generated through Make.\n\nOpen a new tab and log into your Make account, and create a new scenario.\n\nAdd the module Facebook messenger > Watch messages as the first module to your scenario. Click Create a webhook.\n\nEnter a Webhook name and a Verify Token of your choice into the respective fields. You will need this Verify Token value later. Click the Save button.\n\nClicking the save button will generate a URL for your webhook. Copy this URL to your clipboard.\n\nGo back to the Edit Callback URL dialog in your Facebook Developer account. In the Callback URL field, enter the URL from your clipboard, and in the Verify token field, enter the same token that you entered in step 6. Click Verify and Saveto save the dialog.\n\nUnder Generate Access Tokens, click Connect. In the dialog box that opens, choose the pages you want your app to access and click Continue and Save.\n\nClick Got it. You will return to the Generate access tokens section.\n\nFor your chosen page, click Generate.\n\nIn the Token Generated dialog box, confirm that you understand and then copy the token to your clipboard.\n\nTo create a connection between Make and Facebook messenger, add a Send a Message module and click Create a connection. Enter the access token from the previous step into the Access Token field and click Save.\n\nMap the Sender ID to the Page Scoped User ID field and specify the Message Text in the Send a Message module.\n\nSet up the Send a Message module and run the scenario to test your bot.\n\nTesting the Facebook Messenger Bot\nFacebook Messenger\nConnect Facebook Messenger to Make\nHow to create a bot and connect it to Facebook Messenger and Make\nTesting the Facebook Messenger Bot\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationEmail (legacy)\nEmail (legacy)\nGetting started with Email\n\nWith the above modules, you can download emails via IMAP, send emails via SMTP, create new drafts, move and copy emails from one folder to another folder, mark emails as read or unread, and delete emails.\n\nConnecting Email to Make\nIMAP connection settings\n\nThe IMAP connection allows you to access your mailbox remotely and read or manipulate messages in your mailbox. The IMAP connection is used by most of the Email modules. In order to create a connection, follow the general instructions for Connecting an application. Before you click the Continue button, select the type of connection you want to establish (IMAP or Google). These are both IMAP connections. However, Google Gmail requires a different type of authorization.\n\nConnecting to Gmail\n\nWhen choosing the type of connection, select the Google option. After you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Google website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account:\n\nHere, allow access by clicking the Allow button. Afterwards, you will be redirected back to the Make administration page. Now, you can create scenarios with the Email modules that require IMAP connection to your Gmail.\n\nConnecting to other mailboxes via IMAP\n\nWhen choosing the type of connection, select the IMAP option. In the next step, you need to set all the parameters necessary for connecting to your mailbox. The easiest way is to locate your email service provider in the displayed list and select it. When you do this, Make will only require you to provide your mailbox password and username. If your provider is not on the list, select the Other option and specify your host, port, and connection security type. To find this information, check the Help section for your mailbox. If you don’t have this information available, contact your email service provider.\n\nSMTP connection settings\n\nA SMTP connection allows Make to send emails. In order to create a connection, follow the general instructions for Connecting an application. Before you click the Continue button, select the type of connection you want to establish (SMTP or Google). These are both SMTP connections. However, Google Gmail requires a different type of authorization.\n\nConnecting to Gmail\n\nWhen choosing a type of connection, select the Google option. After you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Google website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account:\n\nHere, allow the access by clicking the Allow button. Afterwards, you will be redirected back to the Make administration page. Now, you can create scenarios with Email modules that require IMAP connection to your Gmail.\n\nConnecting to other mailboxes via SMTP\n\nWhen choosing the type of connection, select the SMTP option. In the next step, you need to set all the parameters necessary for connecting to your mailbox. The easiest way is to locate your email service provider in the displayed list and select it. When you do this, Make will only require you to provide your mailbox username and password. If your provider is not on the list, select the Other option and specify your host, port, and connection security type. To find this information, check the Help section for your mailbox. If you don’t have this information available, contact your email service provider.\n\nThe Unique Email ID in IMAP protocol\n\nThe Unique Email ID known as 'Email ID (UID)' is the email's identifier. The Email ID is specific for each of the email's folders. Hint: For getting and deleting the same email from the same folder, you can see below:\n\nGetting an email from the 'Inbox' folder\n\nDeleting the email from the 'Inbox' folder\n\nChanging the displayed name of the sender\n\n1. Open the Send an email action advanced settings using the checkbox \n\n2. Enter the required sender name or email\n\nUse the correct syntax as shown in the hint on the screenshot below. name@email.com or \"Name\" name@email.com\n\nEmail (legacy)\nGetting started with Email\nConnecting Email to Make\nThe Unique Email ID in IMAP protocol\nChanging the displayed name of the sender\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationChatdata\nChatdata\n\nWith Chatdata modules in Make, you can manage the chatbots, send messages, and retrieve the leads in your Chatdata account.\n\nTo use the Chatdata modules, you must have a paid Chatdata account. You can create an account at chat-data.com. For subscription information, refer to the Chatdata Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the Chatdata API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Chatdata to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Chatdata.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Chatdata\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Chatdata account:\n\nLog in to your Chatdata account.\n\nIn the top right corner, click your Username > Account Settings.\n\nIn the API Keys section, click Create a new secret key.\n\nCopy the API key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Key field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Chatdata in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Chatdata module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Chatdata modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Chatdata Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nAction\n\nSend a message\n\nGet the Leads\n\nGet the Conversations\n\nChatbot\n\nCreate a Chatbot\n\nRetrain a Chatbot\n\nUpdate the base prompt\n\nGet the Chatbot training status\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nChatdata\nConnect Chatdata to Make\nObtain your API key in Chatdata\nEstablish the connection with Chatdata in Make\nBuild Chatdata Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationClickatell\nClickatell\n\nThe Clickatell modules enable you to monitor new SMS, create a new SMS, or perform a custom API call in your Clickatell account.\n\nGetting Started with Clickatell\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Clickatell account\n\nIn order to use Clickatell with Make, it is necessary to have a Clickatell account. If you do not have one, you can create a Clickatell account at www.clickatell.com/sign-up.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Clickatell to Make\n\nTo connect your Clickatell account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your Clickatell account.\n\nLog in to your Clickatell account.\n\nGo to SMS > Configure SMS. Add test phone to test the sending and/or receiving of messages from the Sandbox environment.\n\nClick the Create new integration button.\n\nEnter the name of the integration, select the environment (for testing purposes select the Sandbox option),and the REST API Type. Click Next.\n\nSelect the desired features. Click Next.\n\nSwitch on the Enable delivery notifications option to set up the webhook. For more details about the webhook see the Watch New SMS section. Click Next.\n\nSelect your test phone.\n\nSave the integration setting by clicking the Finish button.\n\nClick the Integration you have created and copy the provided API Key.\n\nNote\n\nMake sure that you copy the API Key without space after the key.\n\nGo to Make and open the Clickatell module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nEnter the API Key you have copied in step 9 to the respective field and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nTriggers\nWatch New SMS\nActions\nCreate an SMS\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get a Balance\nClickatell\nGetting Started with Clickatell\nConnecting Clickatell to Make\nTriggers\nWatch New SMS\nActions\nCreate an SMS\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get a Balance\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationChatforma\nChatforma\n\nThe Chatforma modules allow you to monitor new inputs, send messages, add, delete the users in a segment, and list bots, forms, users, messages, segments, dialogue users, and user messages in your Chatforma account.\n\nGetting Started with Chatforma\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Chatforma account\n\nIn order to use Chatforma with Make, it is necessary to have a Chatforma account. If you do not have one, you can create a Chatforma account at chatforma.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Chatforma to Make\n\nTo connect your Chatforma account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your Chatforma account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your Chatforma account.\n\nClick My Profile > Profile > Integration > Create a token.\n\nEnter a name for the token and click Create.\n\nCopy the token to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the Chatforma module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the token copied in step 4, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Chatforma account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative tohttps://api.pro.chatforma.com/public. For example: /v1/bots.\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Chatforma API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we've already done that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Bots\n\nThe following API call returns all the bots from your Chatforma account:\n\nURL:\n\n/v1/bots\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body.\n\nIn our example, 3 bots were returned:\n\nChatforma\nGetting Started with Chatforma\nConnecting Chatforma to Make\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Bots\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

modified calls, SMS, users, trackers, companies, and calls in your CallRail account.\n\nGetting Started with CallRail\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA CallRail account\n\nIn order to use CallRail with Make, it is necessary to have a CallRail account. If you do not have one, you can create a CallRail account at callrail.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting CallRail to Make\n\nTo connect your CallRail account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your CallRail account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your CallRail account.\n\nClick Your Account Name > My Profile > API Keys > Create API V3 Key.\n\nCopy the API Key to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the CallRail module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API Key copied in step 3.\n\nIn the Account ID field, enter your 9-digit account ID without any special characters. You can find the Account ID when you click Your Account Name. For example, 713863719.\n\nClick Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\n\nSee the Setting Up the CallRail Webhooks to add the webhook in your CallRail account.\n\nWatch Pre-Call\nWatch Modified Call\nWatch SMS Received\nWatch SMS Sent\nWatch Trackers\nWatch Companies\nWatch Users\nOther\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CallRail account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.callrail.com/. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Companies\n\nThe following API call returns all the companies from your CallRail account:\n\nURL\n\n/v3/a/Account_ID/companies.json\n\nMethod\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > companies.\n\nIn our example, 5 companies were returned:\n\nWatch Calls\nSetting Up the CallRail Webhooks\n\nOpen any Watch module, enter the details as provided in the respective module, click Save and copy the URL address to your clipboard.\n\nLog in to your CallRail account. Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationApple iOS\nApple iOS\n\nThe Apple iOS modules allow you to monitor events performed by your Apple iOS device and/or perform various actions using your Apple iOS device.\n\nGetting Started With the Apple iOS App\n\nPrerequisites\n\nApple iPhone or iPad\n\nMake App for iOS installed on your device.\n\nIn order to use the Apple iOS app with Make, it is necessary to have the Make for iOS app installed on your device. To install the app, please follow the download instructions, and install the app from the App Store.\n\nhttps://apps.apple.com/us/app/integromat/id1177073656\n\nYou need to log in and register the device with your account. You can only log in by scanning a QR code or manually entering a code into the app. You create the code in your browser when you pair your app with your account on the Devices tab. Once paired, the app shows a list of functions available for your mobile device.\n\nThe module dialog fields in bold in the scenario editor are mandatory!\n\nAdding Your Device to Make Account\n\nTo use the Make for Apple iOS app, you need to add your Apple iOS device to your Make account.\n\nTo add your Apple iOS device to your Make account, please see the Devices documentation article.\n\nSetting Up the Make for iOS App\n\nBefore you can create a scenario using the Apple iOS app modules, you need to set your Make for iOS app to allow access to your device's corresponding functions.\n\nOpen the Make for iOS app and tap Settings.\n\nTap the function you want to use in your scenarios. For example, Photos.\n\nEnable or customize the configuration and tap Setting.\n\nYou can now see the active functions listed under the function title.\n\nUsing the app\n\nThe app is designed to run in the background and perform selected functions. On the main screen, you can switch between two lists: Events and History. The Events include a list of captured events that have not yet been sent to the server. The History contains all events that have already been sent to the server and those that generated an error when being sent. By clicking on an event, you can view its details, including errors that have possibly occurred.\n\nThe app synchronizes events automatically. The synchronization is performed in the shortest possible time interval supported by the operating system. Although for Android devices, events are sent immediately, for iOS devices it can take several hours to send events. The automatic synchronization also occurs every time you open the app. To start the synchronization manually, drag the list of events down.\n\nGeneral Settings\n\nSynchronize events in the order they were created\n\n\t\n\nThis option allows you to keep the synchronization order even if the scenario is not available. No new events are processed until the first event in the queue is processed.\n\n\n\n\nSend photos only over WiFi\n\n\t\n\nWhen enabled, photos will be sent only when your device is connected to the Internet via WiFi. This prevents high data consumption when connected via the mobile data network.\n\nContacts\n\nSend changes in contacts to Make\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to trigger the Watch contacts module in your scenario when the contact is added or updated on the device.\n\n\n\n\nAllow Make to import contacts to the device\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Create a contact module in your scenario to create a contact in your iOS device.\n\n\n\n\nSend All\n\n\t\n\nTap the button to send all contacts from your device to the Make scenario.\n\nCalendar\n\nAllow Make to import events to the device\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Create a calendar event module in your scenario to create a new calendar event on the iOS device.\n\n\n\n\nSend new events to Make\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch a calendar module in your scenario when the calendar event is added or updated on your iOS device.\n\n\n\n\nSend All\n\n\t\n\nTap this button to send all calendar events from your device to the Make scenario.\n\nPhotos\n\nAllow Make to import photos to the device\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to use the Upload a Photo module.\n\n\n\n\nSend new photos to Make\n\n\t\n\nWhen enabled, every time a photo is taken, the app sends the photo to Make and triggers the Watch photos module.\n\nGPS\n\nTriggers\n\nTrack GPS location\n\n\t\n\nActivate this function to trigger the Watch entrances to/exits from a geofence areamodule when the device enters and/or leaves the specified area.\n\nNote\n\nPlease note that you may have to spend a couple of minutes outside/inside the geofence area to trigger this function.\n\n\n\n\nAreas\n\n\t\n\nSet the area you want to watch.\n\nReminders\n\nAllow Make to import reminders to the device\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Create a reminder module in your scenario to create a new reminder on the iOS device.\n\n\n\n\nSend new reminders to Make\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch reminders module in your scenario when a new reminder is added or updated on the device.\n\nNotifications\n\nActions\n\nAllow notifications\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Send a push notification module in your scenario to send a push notification to the selected device.\n\nRunning a scenario using the Make for iOS app\n\nYou can trigger a Makescenario by tapping a button you create in the Make for iOS app.\n\nCreating a button in the iOS app\n\nOpen the Make for iOS app.\n\nTap Buttons.\n\nTap My first button.\n\nEnter the name for your button and ID (you will need this for your Make module), and specify the button properties, if needed.\n\nSave the button by tapping the Save option in the top-right corner.\n\nGo to the Makescenario, and add the Watch Button module to the first position in your scenario.\n\nSelect the device where you have created the button, and enter the ID of the button.\n\nGo back to your Make for iOS app, and tap the button you have created.\n\nTapping the iOS button triggers the Watch Button module. Check the Events tab in the app to confirm whether you tapped the button.\n\nPlacing the Button on Your iOS Screen\n\nSwipe right on your Home screen to view widgets.\n\nScroll down and tap Edit.\n\nTap + in the upper right corner and search for 'Make'.\n\nSearch for Make and find the widget you want on your screen. You can choose between 1, 4, or 8 buttons by swiping left.\n\nConfirm your selection by tapping + Add Widget.\n\nPress the Home button.\n\nThe button now appears on your screen and is available for your scenario.\n\nYou can also place your button on your Apple Watch.\n\nSecurity\n\nTraffic between the mobile device and Make is secured by the Transport Layer Secure (TLS) encryption protocol. The authorization is based on a client certificate that is generated automatically when you log on. The certificate’s private key is generated on the device and securely stored in the System Keychain.\n\nApple iOS\nGetting Started With the Apple iOS App\nAdding Your Device to Make Account\nSetting Up the Make for iOS App\nUsing the app\nGeneral Settings\nContacts\nCalendar\nPhotos\nGPS\nReminders\nNotifications\nRunning a scenario using the Make for iOS app\nCreating a button in the iOS app\nPlacing the Button on Your iOS Screen\nSecurity\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommunicationAndroid\nAndroid\nGetting Started with Android App\n\nThe Android App modules allow you to monitor events performed by your Android phone and/or perform various actions using your Android phone device.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAndroid device (Android 7.0 and higher)\n\nMake App for Android installed on your phone\n\nAs of the beginning of 2019, Google has restricted applications published on Google Play that gives access to:\n\nSMS permissions\n\nCall logs\n\nThe Make app you have downloaded from Google Play is also subject to these restrictions.\n\nInstallation of the Non-restricted Make App for Android\n\nSee the comparison of functions in the restricted and non-restricted app versions.\n\nIn order to install the Make app with no restrictions, follow the steps below:\n\nNote\n\nAll of your settings and scenarios made using the previously installed Make app from Google Play will remain untouched and functional in the new non-restricted Make app for Android.\n\n1. Tap on the following download link, and download the APK file.\n\nMake app for Android (8.5 MB)\n\n2. Open the downloaded make.apk file.\n\nCaution\n\nSome phones (typically Huawei devices) may detect a possible virus in the APK file. There might be various reasons for this to happen. But as we investigated – most likely we are blacklisted by Huawei's antivirus system.\n\nHuawei devices, unlike other OEMs, pre-installed an antivirus into their system and uses Virustotal API (https://developers.virustotal.com/v3.0/reference) which may falsely detect Integromat's APK file as malware. All other OEMs use Google Play Protect anti-malware service where the Integromat app is verified.\n\nIf you are in doubt whether the file contains suspicious software, scan your device using Google Play Protect:\n\nOpen the Google Play Store app ().\n\nAt the top right, tap the profile icon.\n\nTap Play Protect.\n\nTap the Scan button to scan your device for malware and/or viruses.\n\n3. Switch the button to allow the Make app installation.\n\n3. Install the Make application.\n\n4. Open the installed application.\n\n5. Scan the QR code, and proceed to the application.\n\n6. The application is now ready to use.\n\nInstallation of the Restricted Make App for Android on Google Play\n\nYou can still install the Make app for Android on Google Play.\n\nUsing the App\n\nThe app is designed to run in the background and perform selected functions.\n\nOn the main screen, you can switch between the following options:\n\nEvents: Contains a list of captured events that have not yet been sent to the server. The app synchronizes events automatically. The synchronization is performed in the shortest possible time interval supported by the operating system. While for Android devices, events are sent immediately, for iOS devices, it can take several hours to send events. The automatic synchronization also occurs every time you open the app. To start the synchronization manually, drag the list of events down.\n\nHistory: Contains all events that have already been sent to the server and those that generated an error when being sent. By clicking on an event, you can view its details, including any errors that have possibly occurred.\n\nButtons: Buttons allow you to run a scenario by tapping the associated button on your Android device.\n\nScanner: Use the barcode or QR code scanner to scan respective codes and trigger the scenario.\n\nSettings: Settings of the Make for Android app features.\n\nModules are divided into two categories: triggers and actions. Triggers have the ability to listen to the connected device and start the scenario whenever the device generates a new event. Actions, on the other hand, create new items in the device. Select the desired trigger or action, and add it to your scenario. In the configuration window of the module, select the desired module and, where appropriate, set up other parameters.\n\nSetting Up the Make for Android App\n\nBefore you start building a scenario using the Android app modules,you need to set up your Make for the Android app to allow the app access to your phone's corresponding functions.\n\nGeneral Settings\n\nSynchronize events in the order they were created\n\n\t\n\nThis option allows you to keep the synchronization order even if the scenario is not available. No new events are processed until the first event in the queue is processed.\n\n\n\n\nSend photos only over WiFi\n\n\t\n\nWhen enabled, photos will be sent only when your device is connected to the Internet via WiFi. It prevents high data consumption when connected via the mobile data network.\n\n\n\n\nDark Mode\n\n\t\n\nYou can switch the Make app for Android to Dark Mode or Light Mode.\n\nSelect one of the options:\n\nAlways light: Switches the app to the Light Mode.\n\nAlways dark: Switches the app to the Dark Mode.\n\nFollow system: The mode is selected according to your system settings.\n\nQR / Barcode Scanner\n\nSame code scan delay\n\n\t\n\nSet the period when the same code is scanned again.\n\n\n\n\nDefault description\n\n\t\n\nEnter the description to be added to all scanned codes.\n\nYou must have descriptions enabled to use a default description.\n\nPhotos\n\nTriggers\n\nSend new photos to Make\n\n\t\n\nWhen enabled, every time a photo is taken, the app sends the photo to Make, and then triggers the New Photo module.\n\nActions\n\nAllow Make to import photos to the device\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to allow the use of the Save a Photo module.\n\n\n\n\nTake photo\n\n\t\n\nAllows you to use the Take a Photo module.\n\nGPS\n\nTriggers\n\nTrack GPS location\n\n\t\n\nAllows you to use the Watch location changes module that triggers when the device changes location. Use the Change button to define the distance that has to be changed to trigger the event.\n\n\n\n\nEntered/left area\n\n\t\n\nActivate this function to send information when the device enters and/or leaves the specified area to the Watch entrances to/exits from a geofence area module.\n\nPlease note that you must spend a couple of minutes outside/inside the geofence area to trigger this function.\n\nWiFi\n\nTriggers\n\nWifi connected event\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the WiFi connection module in your scenario when the device connects to the WiFi network.\n\n\n\n\nWifi disconnected event\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the WiFi disconnection module when the device disconnects from the WiFi network.\n\nActions\n\nEnable WiFi\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Enable Wifi module in your scenario.\n\n\n\n\nDisable WiFi\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Disable Wifi module in your scenario.\n\nBluetooth\n\nTriggers\n\nBluetooth enabled\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Bluetooth activations module in your scenario when Bluetooth is enabled on your device.\n\n\n\n\nBluetooth disabled\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Bluetooth Deactivations module in your scenario when Bluetooth is disabled on your device.\n\n\n\n\nDevice connected\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch connections from Bluetooth Devices module in your scenario when your Bluetooth device connects to another device.\n\n\n\n\nDevice disconnected\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Disconnections from Bluetooth Devices module in your scenario when your Bluetooth device disconnects from another device.\n\nActions\n\nEnable bluetooth\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Enable Bluetooth module in your scenario to turn on Bluetooth on your device.\n\n\n\n\nDisable bluetooth\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Disable Bluetooth module in your scenario to turn off Bluetooth on your device.\n\nCalls\n\nCall functions (except Change a Ring Mode) are available for the non-restricted Make for Android app only.\n\nTriggers\n\nIncoming call\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Incoming Calls module in your scenario when your device registers an incoming call.\n\n\n\n\nIncoming call ended\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Completed Incoming Calls module in your scenario when an incoming call is finished.\n\n\n\n\nOutgoing call\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Outgoing Calls module in your scenario when your device makes an outgoing call.\n\n\n\n\nOutgoing call ended\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Completed Outgoing Calls module in your scenario when an outgoing call is finished.\n\nActions\n\nPrepare phone call\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Prepare a Phone Call module in your scenario to display the pre-defined phone number in the phone's dialer app.\n\n\n\n\nMake Call\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Make a Call module in your scenario to dial the phone number specified in the Make a Call module.\n\n\n\n\nChange ringmode\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Change a Ring Mode module in your scenario to switch the ring mode between silent, vibration, and loud ring modes.\n\nSMS\nCaution\n\nSMS functions are available for the non-restricted Make for Android app only.\n\nTriggers\n\nNew SMS received\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Watch Text Messages module in your scenario when your device receives an SMS.\n\n\n\n\nNew SMS sent\n\n\t\n\nThis function triggers the Sent SMS module in your scenario when your device sends an SMS.\n\nActions\n\nSend SMS\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Send Text Message module in your scenario to send a text message. The recipient number and the text message content must be entered into the respective fields of the Send Text Message module.\n\nWeb\n\nActions\n\nOpen websites\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Open a Web Browser module in your scenario to open a specified URL address in a web browser on your device.\n\n\n\n\nClose websites\n\n\t\n\nThis function allows you to use the Close a Web Browser module in your scenario to close a web browser on your device.\n\nRunning a scenario Using the Make for Android App\n\nYou can run the Make scenario by tapping the button created in the Android app.\n\nThe button can be placed as a widget on your Android screen.\n\nCreating the Button in the Android App\n\nOpen the Make for the Android app.\n\nTap Buttons.\n\nTap My first button.\n\nEnter the name for your button and ID (you will need this for your Make module), and customize the button color and icon as you like.\n\nSave the button by tapping Done.\n\nCreate or go to a Make scenario, and add the Android>Watch Button module to the first position in your scenario.\n\nSelect the device where you have created the button, and enter the ID of the button.\n\nYou can test the button by right-clicking on the Android>Watch Button module and clicking Run this module only.\n\nThen tap the button on your Android device.\n\nThe Watch Button module in your scenario is triggered. Now, you can use this function to trigger your scenario via your mobile device.\n\nPlacing the Button on Your Android Screen\n\nTap and hold anywhere on your Android screen to open the Manage Home menu.\n\nTap Widgets.\n\nFind and tap the Make app.\n\nSelect the widget you want to add to your screen.\n\nThe button now appears on your screen. You can move it by touching and holding the button and then dragging it where you\n\nScanner\n\nBarcode and QR code scanner.\n\nYou can access the QR/barcode scanner by tapping the Scanner button in your app. The Scanner allows you to send barcode/QR code information to the module, and trigger the Make scenario (using Watch Barcode/QR Code module) by scanning a barcode or QR code.\n\nThe scanner features three buttons:\n\nFront/back to switch between your device's cameras.\n\nFlashlight to turn on your device's flashlight as needed.\n\nTag to add descriptions to your scans.\n\nThe Barcode and QR code reader supports the following code formats:\n\nCode 128 (FORMAT_CODE_128)\nCode 39 (FORMAT_CODE_39)\nCode 93 (FORMAT_CODE_93)\nCodabar (FORMAT_CODABAR)\nEAN-13 (FORMAT_EAN_13)\nEAN-8 (FORMAT_EAN_8)\nITF (FORMAT_ITF)\nUPC-A (FORMAT_UPC_A)\nUPC-E (FORMAT_UPC_E)\nQR Code (FORMAT_QR_CODE)\nPDF417 (FORMAT_PDF417)\nAztec (FORMAT_AZTEC)\nData Matrix (FORMAT_DATA_MATRIX)\n\nSecurity\n\nThe traffic between the mobile device and Make is secured by the Transport Layer Secure (TLS) encryption protocol. The authorization is based on a client certificate that is generated automatically when you log on. The certificate’s private key is generated on the device and securely stored in the System Keychain.\n\nAndroid\nGetting Started with Android App\nInstallation of the Non-restricted Make App for Android\nInstallation of the Restricted Make App for Android on Google Play\nUsing the App\nSetting Up the Make for Android App\nGeneral Settings\nQR / Barcode Scanner\nPhotos\nGPS\nWiFi\nBluetooth\nCalls\nSMS\nWeb\nRunning a scenario Using the Make for Android App\nCreating the Button in the Android App\nPlacing the Button on Your Android Screen\nScanner\nSecurity\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

linked accounts, users, and feed events.\n\nTo use the Blink modules, you must have a paid Blink account. You can create an account at joinblink.com. For subscription information, refer to Blink Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the Blink API Documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Blink to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nCreate a Blink app.\n\nObtain your API token in Blink.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nCreate a Blink app\n\nTo create a Blink app you must:\n\nLog in to your Blink account.\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Admin > Manage Apps.\n\nGo to Created Apps.\n\nClick Create app.\n\nEnter a name for the app.\n\nClick Create.\n\nObtain your API token in Blink\n\nTo obtain your API token from your Blink account:\n\nAfter you created the Blink app, scroll down to Technical setup section.\n\nClick Add Token.\n\nCopy the API token value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the Token field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Blink in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Blink module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Token field, enter the API token copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Blink modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Blink Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nFeed Events\n\nSend a Feed Event\n\nUpdate a Feed Event\n\nArchive a Feed Event\n\nGet a Feed Event\n\nList Feed Event Categories\n\nLinked Accounts\n\nGet a Linked Account\n\nList Linked Accounts\n\nUsers\n\nList Users\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nBlink\nConnect Blink to Make\nCreate a Blink app\nObtain your API token in Blink\nEstablish the connection with Blink in Make\nBuild Blink Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

list, and/or delete items, price lists, contacts, estimates, invoices, payments, credit notes, expenses, projects, time entries in your Zoho Invoice account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Zoho Invoice account\n\nIn order to use Zoho Invoice with Make, it is necessary to have a Zoho Invoice account. If you do not have one, you can create a Zoho Invoice account at www.zoho.com/invoice/signup.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Zoho Invoice to Make\n\nTo connect your Zoho Invoice account to Make, you need to obtain your organization ID and region.\n\nLog into your Zoho Invoice Account.\n\nOpen your profile menu in the top-right corner.\n\nClick on the Manage button next to the My Organizations section.\n\nCopy the Organization ID to the clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the Zoho Invoice module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nEnter the Organization ID you have copied in step 4 to the respective field.\n\nSelect the region of your Zoho Invoice account. If the URL of your account is e.g. https://invoice.zoho.eu, then select the EU option.\n\nClick the Continue button.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Accept button.\n\nThe connection has been update, send, retrieve, list, and delete the messages, email templates, contact lists, contacts, and configuration sets in your Amazon SES account.\n\nGetting Started with Amazon SES\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAn Amazon SES account - create an account at aws.amazon.com/ses/\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Amazon SES to Make\n\nTo connect your Amazon SES account to Make you need to obtain the AWS Key, and AWS Secret Key from your Amazon SES account and insert them in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your Amazon SES account.\n\nClick your Account Name > My Security Credentials > Access keys (access key ID and secret access key) > Create New Access Key.\n\nClick Show Access Key to display the Access Key ID and Secret Access Key. Copy and save the provided keys in a safe place.\n\nGo to Make and open the Amazon SES module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the AWS Key and AWS Secret Key fields, enter the Access Key and Secret Access Key values provided in step 3 above.\n\nIn the Region field, select your region and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nMessage\nSend a Message\nEmail Template\nWatch Email Templates\nList Email Templates\nCreate an Email Template\nGet an Email Template\nUpdate an Email Template\nDelete an Email Template\nContact List\nList Contact Lists\nCreate a Contact List\nGet a Contact List\nUpdate a Contact List\nDelete a Contact List\nContact\nWatch Contacts\nList Contacts\nCreate a Contact\nGet a Contact\nUpdate a Contact\nDelete a Contact\nConfiguration Set\nList Configuration Sets\nGet a Configuration Set\nCreate a Configuration Set\nCreate a Configuration Set Event Destination\nDelete a Configuration Set\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Contacts\nAmazon SES\nGetting Started with Amazon SES\nConnecting Amazon SES to Make\nMessage\nSend a Message\nEmail Template\nWatch Email Templates\nList Email Templates\nCreate an Email Template\nGet an Email Template\nUpdate an Email Template\nDelete an Email Template\nContact List\nList Contact Lists\nCreate a Contact List\nGet a Contact List\nUpdate a Contact List\nDelete a Contact List\nContact\nWatch Contacts\nList Contacts\nCreate a Contact\nGet a Contact\nUpdate a Contact\nDelete a Contact\nConfiguration Set\nList Configuration Sets\nGet a Configuration Set\nCreate a Configuration Set\nCreate a Configuration Set Event Destination\nDelete a Configuration Set\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Contacts\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommerceZoho Books\nZoho Books\n\nWith Zoho Books modules in Make, you can create, list, retrieve, update, and delete contacts, persons, invoices, payments, expenses, and bills in your Zoho Books account.\n\nTo get started with Zoho Books, create an account at zoho.com/books/signup.\n\nRefer to the Zoho Books API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Zoho Books to Make\n\nTo connect your Zoho Books account:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Zoho Books module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Region field, select your Zoho account region. For example, US.\n\nOptional: Click Show Advanced Settings, and enter the client credentials from your custom app or add additional scopes. See Create Custom App and Client Credentials for Zoho Books.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou can now edit your scenario and add more Zoho Books modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nCreate Custom App and Client Credentials for Zoho Books\n\nLog in to your Zoho API Console.\n\nClick the + Add Client button and select Server-based Applications.\n\nEnter the details below and click Create.\n\nClient Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the application name you want to register with Zoho.\n\n\n\n\nHomepage URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter your homepage URL, for example, https://www.make.com/en.\n\n\n\n\nAuthorized Redirect URIs\n\n\t\n\nAdd the redirect URI: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/zoho-books.\n\nCopy the Client ID and Client Secret and store them in a safe place.\n\nYou now have the client credentials to connect to Make.\n\nSet Up Zoho Books Webhooks\n\nThe process consists of two main steps:\n\nCreate a Webhook\n\nCreate a Workflow Rule\n\nStep 1: Create a Webhook\n\nAdd a Zoho Books instant module to your scenario and click Create a webhook.\n\nOptional: Enter a name for the webhook in the Webhook name field.\n\nClick Save > Copy address to clipboard.\n\nLog in to your Zoho Books account.\n\nIn the top-right corner, click on the Settings icon > Automation.\n\nFrom the Automation options, select Webhooks, then click the + New Webhook button.\n\nUpdate the following required information (all other fields can be left as the auto-selected defaults):\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the webhook.\n\n\n\n\nModule\n\n\t\n\nSelect the corresponding Module to the instant module you added to your scenario.\n\n\n\n\nURL & Parameters\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Post method and paste the webhook address you copied in Step 3.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnsure the Default Payload option is selected.\n\nClick Save.\n\nStep 2: Create a Workflow Rule\n\nIn the top-right corner of your Zoho Books account, click on the Settings icon > Automation > Workflow Rules.\n\nClick the + New Workflow Rule button in the top-right corner.\n\nEnter the following information:\n\nWorkflow Rule Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the workflow rule.\n\n\n\n\nModule\n\n\t\n\nSelect the corresponding Module to your webhook.\n\n\n\n\nChoose when to Trigger\n\n\t\n\nChoose when to execute the workflow.\n\n\n\n\nFilter the triggers\n\n\t\n\nOptional: add filter criteria for your trigger.\n\n\n\n\nActions\n\n\t\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the Webhooks option.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nSelect the webhook you configured in Step 1: Creating a Webhook.\n\nClick the Save button.\n\nNow, when a specified event is performed, the respective webhook is triggered in your scenario.\n\nPlease see the Zoho Books Automation help for further details about automation functions.\n\nContacts\n\nYou can create, retrieve, list, update, and delete contacts and budgets in a category, and make API calls.\n\nTo get started with YNAB, create an account at YNAB.com.\n\nRefer to the YNAB API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect YNAB to Make\n\nTo connect your YNAB account to Make, you must retrieve a personal access token from your YNAB account.\n\nLog in to your YNAB account and go to your Account Settings page.\n\nScroll down to the Developer Settings section and click the Developer Settings button.\n\nNote: If you have not already confirmed your email, you will receive an email from YNAB to do so.\n\nIf you have not set an account password, click the set an account password link, follow the instructions to do so, then return to the Developer Settings page.\n\nClick the New Token button.\n\nEnter your account password and click the Generate button.\n\nThe token appears at the top of the screen. Copy the token and store it in a safe place as you will not be able to view the token again.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a YNAB module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Personal Access Token field, paste the token copied in Step 5.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more YNAB modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nTransactions\nCreate Transactions\nList Transactions\nCategories\nBudget to a Category\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Transactions\nGetting Started with YNAB\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA YNAB account\n\nIn order to use YNAB with Make, it is necessary to have a YNAB account. Copy the token and store it in a safe place as you will not be able to view the token again.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a YNAB module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Personal Access Token field, paste the token copied in Step 5.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommerceWooCommerce\nWooCommerce\n\nWooCommerce modules in Make, you can monitor, create, retrieve, update, delete, and search coupons, customers, orders, order notes, products, and product attributes, terms, categories, and variations.\n\nTo get started with WooCommerce, you must have a WooCommerce account and a WooCommerce WordPress plugin installed.\n\nRefer to the WooCommerce API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect WooCommerce to Make\n\nTo connect your WooCommerce account to Make,you must generate the Consumer Key and Consumer Secret in your WooCommerce account.\n\nLog in to your WordPress dashboard.\n\nIn the left sidebar, click WooCommerce > Settings.\n\nClick on the Advanced tab.\n\nGo to Legacy API, check the Enable the Legacy REST API checkbox, and click Save changes.\n\nContinue to the REST API section and click the Add Key button.\n\nEnter the description of your connection and select the Read/Write option from the permissions drop-down menu.\n\nClick on the Generate API Key button.\n\nWhen the page refreshes, copy the Consumer Key and Consumer Secret and store them in a safe place.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a WooCommerce module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nIn the Consumer Key and Consumer Secret fields, enter the credentials you copied in Step 8.\n\nIn the Eshop URL field, enter the URL of your Eshop, including HTTPS. For example, https://my-eshop.com.\n\nClick Save.\n\nNote\n\nSSL must be enabled on your WordPress site.\n\nNote\n\nUse pretty permalinks. Change the permalinks settings under Settings > Permalinks.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more WooCommerce modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nTriggers\n\n(Reference: https://woocommerce.github.io/woocommerce-rest-api-docs/)\n\nNew event\nWatch Coupons\nWatch Customers\nWatch Orders\nWatch Products\nAction\nCreate a Coupon\nCreate a Customer\nCreate an Order\nCreate an Order Note\nCreate a Product\nCreate Products (batch)\nCreate a Product Variation\nDelete a coupon\nDelete a Customer\nDelete an Order\nDelete an Order Note\nDelete a Product\nDelete Products (batch)\nDelete a Product Variation\nGet a Coupon\nGet a Customer\nGet an Order\nGet an Order Note\nGet a Product\nGet a Product Variation\nUpdate a Coupon\nUpdate a Customer\nUpdate an Order\nUpdate an Order Status\nUpdate a Product\nUpdate a Product Variation\nSearches\nSearch for a Customer\nList Order Notes\nList Product Variations\nSearch for a Coupon\nSearch for an Order\nSearch for a Product\nWooCommerce\nConnect WooCommerce to Make\nTriggers\nNew event\nWatch Coupons\nWatch Customers\nWatch Orders\nWatch Products\nAction\nCreate a Coupon\nCreate a Customer\nCreate an Order\nCreate an Order Note\nCreate a Product\nCreate Products (batch)\nCreate a Product Variation\nDelete a coupon\nDelete a Customer\nDelete an Order\nDelete an Order Note\nDelete a Product\nDelete Products (batch)\nDelete a Product Variation\nGet a Coupon\nGet a Customer\nGet an Order\nGet an Order Note\nGet a Product\nGet a Product Variation\nUpdate a Coupon\nUpdate a Customer\nUpdate an Order\nUpdate an Order Status\nUpdate a Product\nUpdate a Product Variation\nSearches\nSearch for a Customer\nList Order Notes\nList Product Variations\nSearch for a Coupon\nSearch for an Order\nSearch for a Product\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommerceSyncro\nSyncro\n\nThe Syncro modules allow you to monitor, create, update, list, and delete the customers, tickets, and leads in your Syncro account.\n\nGetting Started with Syncro\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Syncro account\n\nIn order to use Syncro with Make, it is necessary to have a Syncro account. If you do not have one, you can create a Syncro account at syncromsp.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Syncro to Make\n\nTo connect your Syncro account to Make you need to obtain the Access Token from your Syncro account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your Syncro account.\n\n2. Click Your Profile Icon > Settings > API Tokens > New Token > Custom Permissions.\n\n3. Enter a name for the token, select permissions, and click Create API Token.\n\n4. Copy the API token to your clipboard and store it in a safe place.\n\n5. Go to Make and open the Syncro module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n6. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n7. In the Domain Name field, enter your Syncro account's URL address domain name. For example, if your account's URL is https://www.xyz.syncromsp.com, then the domain is xyz.\n\n8. In the Access Token field, enter the token copied in step 4, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established,\n\nCustomers\n\nSee Setting Up Syncro Webhooks to add webhooks to your Syncro account.\n\nWatch New Customer\nSearch Customer\nGet a Customer\nCreate a Customer\nUpdate a Customer\nDelete a Customer\nTickets\n\nSee Setting Up Syncro Webhooks to add webhooks in your Syncro account.\n\nWatch Ticket\nSearch Tickets\nGet a Ticket\nCreate a Ticket\nUpdate a Ticket\nDelete a Ticket\nLeads\nSearch Leads\nGet a Lead\nCreate a Lead\nUpdate a Lead\nInvoices and Payments\n\nSee Setting Up Syncro Webhooks to add webhooks in your Syncro account.\n\nWatch New Invoice\nWatch New Payment\nRMM\n\nSee Setting Up Syncro Webhooks to add webhooks in your Syncro account.\n\nWatch New RMM Alert\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Customers\nSetting Up Syncro Webhooks\n\n1. Open any Watch module, enter a name for the webhook, and click Save. Copy the URL address to your clipboard and save the trigger.\n\n2. Log in to your Syncro account. Click Your Account Name > Settings > Notifications Center > New Notification Set.\n\n3. Enter a name for the webhook, select the users to notify about the event, in the Webhook URL field, enter the URL address copied in step 1, and select the events for which you want to receive the notifications.\n\n4. Click Create Notification Set.\n\nThe webhook is successfully created. You will receive notifications when a new customer is created.\n\nSyncro\nGetting Started with Syncro\nConnecting Syncro to Make\nCustomers\nWatch New Customer\nSearch Customer\nGet a Customer\nCreate a Customer\nUpdate a Customer\nDelete a Customer\nTickets\nWatch Ticket\nSearch Tickets\nGet a Ticket\nCreate a Ticket\nUpdate a Ticket\nDelete a Ticket\nLeads\nSearch Leads\nGet a Lead\nCreate a Lead\nUpdate a Lead\nInvoices and Payments\nWatch New Invoice\nWatch New Payment\nRMM\nWatch New RMM Alert\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get Customers\nSetting Up Syncro Webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

retrieve, list, and the expenses in your Splitwise account.\n\nGetting Started with Splitwise\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Splitwise account\n\nIn order to use Splitwise with Make, it is necessary to have a Splitwise account. Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommerceTripletex\nTripletex\n\nWith the Tripletex modules in Make, you can retrieve, create, update, search and/or delete aspects of timesheets, ledgers, projects, invoices, orders, customers, products, logistics settings, timesheet settings, and historical vouchers and make API calls.\n\nTripletex provides two types of environments that you can connect to in Make: Production and Sandbox.\n\nNote\n\nRefer to the Tripletex API documentation for the list of available endpoints.\n\nProduction Environment\n\nTo use the Tripletex Production environment, you must have an account at tripletex.no. To set up integrations in the Production environment, your account must have the Smart package subscription or higher.\n\nSandbox Environment\n\nTo use the Tripletex Staging environment and test the API, you can create an account at tripletex.io. After submitting the form, Tripletex generates Sandbox credentials that you will use to connect to Make.\n\nWhen you are ready to switch from the Sandbox environment to the Production environment, apply for access to the API in Production by filling out this Tripletex form. Please note that Tripletex's process may take up to 2-3 weeks and you will receive a new set of Production credentials. Refer to the Tripletex Getting Started guide for more information.\n\nConnect Tripletex to Make\n\nTo connect to the Production environment, you must have an employee token. Only Tripletex accounts with administrator rights can create employee tokens.\n\nTo connect to the Sandbox environment, you must have the employee and consumer tokens that were provided when you registered at Tripletex. These credentials can only be used in the Sandbox environment.\n\nTo connect to the Tripletex app:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Tripletex module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Employee Token field, enter your employee token.\n\nProduction Environment: This token is created by an administrator account in Tripletex. For instructions on how to create this token, refer to the Create an Employee Token in Tripletex section below.\n\nSandbox Environment: This token is generated when you register for access to the Sandbox environment.\n\nSelect Yes or No in the Sandbox field to choose the environment to connect to.\n\nSandbox Environment: Enter the Consumer Token generated when you registered for access to Sandbox environment.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Tripletex modules. If your connection needs reauthorization, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nCreate an Employee Token in Tripletex\nNote\n\nYou must have administrator rights in Tripletex to create an employee token.\n\nTo create an employee token:\n\nLog in to your Tripletex account.\n\nClick Company > Employees on the left sidebar.\n\nClick on the employee you are generating the token for.\n\nClick on the API access tab > New token.\n\nSelect Make in the Application field, enter a name for the token, and click Create token.\n\nCopy the API token that appears, store it in a safe place as you cannot view the token again, and click OK.\n\nClick on the name of the token you just created in the API employee tokens list.\n\nSelect the desired access types for the token.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully created the employee token to establish the connection in Scenario. Return to the Connect Tripletex to Make section to continue establishing the connection.\n\nBuild Tripletex Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTimesheet and/or delete order events, shipment events, funds, tag to order, assign users to order, warehouses, carriers, customers, products, and stores in your ShipStation account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA ShipStation account\n\nIn order to use ShipStation with Make, it is necessary to have a ShipStation account. Log in to your ShipStation account.\n\n2. Click on the account icon in the top menu bar, and then choose My Profile... from the dropdown menu.\n\n3. In the left side bar, click on API Settings.\n\n4. Click Generate New API Keys button to receive the API Key and API Secret or copy the API Key and API Secret from the API Keys section.\n\n5. Go to Make and open the ShipStation module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n6. Enter the API Key and API Secret you have copied in step 3 to the respective field.\n\n7. Click the Continue button.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\nListen for Order Events\nListen for Order Events (with Item Info)\nListen for Shipment Events\nListen for Shipment Events (With Item Info)\nActions\nAdd Funds\nAdd Tag to Order\nAssign User to Order\nCreate Order\nCreate Warehouse\nDeactivate Store\nDelete Order\nGet Carrier\nGet Customer\nGet Order\nGet Product\nGet Store\nGet Warehouse\nMark an Order as Shipped\nReactivate Store\nRefresh Store\nRemove Tag From Order\nUnassign User from Order\nUpdate Order\nUpdate Product\nUpdate Store\nUpdate Warehouse\nVoid Label\nSearches\nList Carriers\nList Customers\nList Fulfillments\nList Marketplaces\nList Orders\nList Packages\nList Products\nList Services\nList Shipments\nList Stores\nList Tags\nList Users\nList Warehouses\nShipStation\nConnecting ShipStation to Make\nTriggers\nListen for Order Events\nListen for Order Events (with Item Info)\nListen for Shipment Events\nListen for Shipment Events (With Item Info)\nActions\nAdd Funds\nAdd Tag to Order\nAssign User to Order\nCreate Order\nCreate Warehouse\nDeactivate Store\nDelete Order\nGet Carrier\nGet Customer\nGet Order\nGet Product\nGet Store\nGet Warehouse\nMark an Order as Shipped\nReactivate Store\nRefresh Store\nRemove Tag From Order\nUnassign User from Order\nUpdate Order\nUpdate Product\nUpdate Store\nUpdate Warehouse\nVoid Label\nSearches\nList Carriers\nList Customers\nList Fulfillments\nList Marketplaces\nList Orders\nList Packages\nList Products\nList Services\nList Shipments\nList Stores\nList Tags\nList Users\nList Warehouses\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

product variants, product images, collects, custom collections, customers, articles, pages, refunds, fulfillments, fulfillment orders, fulfillment services, inventories, abandoned checkouts, transations, discounts, metafields, payments, and themes in your Shopify account.\n\nTo use the Shopify modules, you must have a Shopify account. You can create an account at www.shopify.com/signup.\n\nRefer to the Shopify API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnecting Shopify to Make\n\nShopify offers two types of connections:\n\nStandard OAuth connection (displayed as Shopify in the Create connection dialog) - use this by default\n\nCustom app (displayed as Shopify (custom or private apps)) - use this if the standard connection does not work\n\nTo connect your Shopify account to Make, follow these steps:\n\nConnecting Shopify using the standard connection type\n\nUse the Shopify connection type by default. If creating the connection causes errors, use the custom or private app connection type.\n\nInsert a Shopify module into a scenario. Under Connection, click Add.\n\nThe Create a Connection dialog appears.\n\nIn the Connection type, select Shopify.\n\nType a Connection name.\n\nEnter the Myshopify.com subdomain of your store.\n\nFor example, if the URL of your store is https://mystore.myshopify.com, the subdomain to enter in the connection dialog is mystore.\n\nClick Save.\n\nThe system opens Shopify in a new window. Shopify asks you to log in and install the Make app and approve its access to your store data.\n\nIn the Shopify Install dialog, review the privacy and permissions details, and then click Install unlisted app.\n\nConnecting Shopify using a Shopify private or custom app\n\nUse the Shopify (custom or private app) connection type if the standard Shopify connection type does not work for you.\n\nThis connection type requires creating a custom app in your Shopify store.\n\nLog in to your Shopify store, click Apps, then click App and sales channel settings.\n\nOn the Apps and channels screen, click Develop apps.\n\nClick Allow custom app development, then confirm this action again by clicking Allow custom app development on the next screen.\n\nThis will allow you to create an API token that you will use when creating the connection in Make.\n\nClick Create an app.\n\nType an App name, select an App developer, and click Create app.\n\nClick Configuration, then click Configure next to Admin API integration.\n\nOn the Admin API integration screen, select scopes (permissions) that represent the actions you will need Make to perform. Then click Save.\n\nSwitch to the API credentials tab and under Access tokens, click Install app. In the dialog that appears, confirm the action by clicking Install app.\n\nShopify creates an Admin API access token. Click Reveal token once and copy the token. You will enter this token into Make in the next step.\n\nIn Make, add a Shopify module to a scenario. Under Connection, click Add, then fill in the required details shown in the following image.\n\nClick Save.\n\nPublic App Connection\nPrivate App Connection\nBuild Shopify Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nOrders\n\nCreate an Order\n\nCreate a Draft Order\n\nNote: In the output, the Shipping Line field is sometimes empty because the user must have at least one item in the item list that requires shipping.\n\nIf not specified, the item is treated as not requiring shipping, and Shopify ignores Shipping Lines.\n\nImport a B2B Order\n\nOnly available for stores on the Shopify Plus plan.\n\nUpdate an Order\n\nDelete an Order\n\nClose an Order\n\nReopen an Order\n\nCancel an Order\n\nGet an Order\n\nCount Orders\n\nSearch for connection to your Sage Business Cloud Accounting account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.accounting.sage.com/. For example, /v3.1/addresses.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of use - Search Products\n\nThe following API call returns all the products from your account.\n\nURL: /v3.1/products\n\nMethod: GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > items. \n\nIn our example 124 products were returned:\n\nSage Business Cloud Accounting\nConnect Sage Business Cloud Accounting to Make\nSales Quotes\nWatch Sales Quotes\nCreate a Sales Quote\nUpdate a Sales Quote\nGet a Sales Quote\nSearch Sales Quotes\nDelete a Sales Quote\nSales Invoices\nWatch Sales Invoice\nCreate a Sales Invoice\nUpdate a Sales Invoice\nGet a Sales Invoice\nSearch Sales Invoice\nVoid a Sales Invoice\nPurchase Invoices\nWatch Purchase Invoices\nCreate a Purchase Invoice\nUpdate a Purchase Invoice\nGet a Purchase Invoice\nSearch Purchase Invoices\nDelete a Purchase Invoice\nCustomers\nWatch Customers\nCreate a Customer\nUpdate a Customer\nGet a Customer\nSearch Customers\nDelete a Customer\nContact Payments\nWatch Contact Payments\nCreate a Contact Payment\nUpdate a Contact Payment\nGet a Contact Payment\nSearch Contact Payments\nDelete a Contact Payment\nProducts\nWatch Products\nCreate a Product\nUpdate a Product\nGet a Product\nSearch Products\nDelete a Product\nServices\nWatch Services\nCreate a Service\nUpdate a Service\nGet a Service\nSearch Services\nDelete a Service\nStock Items\nWatch Stock Items\nCreate a Stock Item\nUpdate a Stock Item\nGet a Stock Item\nSearch Stock Items\nDelete a Stock Item\nOther\nMake an API Call\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

monitor, retrieve, create and delete payment drafts in your Revolut Business account.\n\nNotice\n\nDue to Revolut's restrictions, the Payment Drafts endpoints are accessible via Revolut API.\n\nGetting Started with Revolut Business\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Revolut Business account — you can create one at business.revolut.com.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Revolut Business to Make\n\n1. Go to Make and open the Revolut Business module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n2. Enter a name for the connection to the Connection name field and click Continue.\n\n3. After you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Revolut Business website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\n4. Confirm the dialog by clicking the Authorise button.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nDraft Payments\nWatch Draft Payments\nList Draft Payments\nGet a Draft Payment\nCreate a Draft Payment\nDelete a Draft Payment\nDelete a Draft Payment Transfer\nRevolut Business v3\nGetting Started with Revolut Business\nConnecting Revolut Business to Make\nDraft Payments\nWatch Draft Payments\nList Draft Payments\nGet a Draft Payment\nCreate a Draft Payment\nDelete a Draft Payment\nDelete a Draft Payment Transfer\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsCommerceSalla\nSalla\n\nWith Salla modules in Make, you can manage the products, orders, brands and categories in your Salla account.\n\nTo use the Salla modules, you must have a Salla account. You can create an account at salla.com.\n\nRefer to the Salla API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Salla to Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Salla module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nOptional: Click Show advanced settings and enter your custom app client credentials. For more information, refer to Salla Private App Guide.\n\nIf requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/salla.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Salla modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Salla Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nProduct\n\nAttach Image To Product\n\nCreate a Product\n\nDelete a Product\n\nSearch Products\n\nUpdate Product\n\nUpdate Product Quantity\n\nWatch Product Available\n\nWatch Product Created\n\nWatch Product Deleted\n\nOrder\n\nWatch Order Cancelled\n\nWatch Order Coupon Updated\n\nWatch Order Created\n\nWatch Order Customer Updated\n\nWatch Order Deleted\n\nWatch Order Payment Updated\n\nWatch Order Products Updated\n\nWatch Order Refunded\n\nWatch Order Updated\n\nBrand\n\nCreate a Brand\n\nDelete a Brand\n\nSearch Brands\n\nUpdate a Brand\n\nWatch Brand Created\n\nWatch Brand Deleted\n\nWatch Brand Updated\n\nCategory\n\nCreate a Category\n\nDelete a Category\n\nUpdate a Category\n\nWatch Category Created\n\nWatch Category Updated\n\nOther\n\nCustom Webhook\n\nSearch Categories\n\nSearch Customers\n\nWatch Abandoned Cart\n\nWatch Coupon Applied\n\nWatch Customer Created\n\nWatch Customer Login\n\nWatch Customer Otp Request\n\nWatch Customer Updated\n\nWatch Review Added\n\nWatch Special Offer Created\n\nWatch Special Offer Updated\n\nWatch Store Tax Created\n\nYour Custom Action\n\nMake an API Call\n\nNote\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nWhen you create a Salla webhook in Make, it is attached automatically and requires no additional set up.\n\nSalla\nConnect Salla to Make\nBuild Salla Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
